Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Introduction to the Principles of Recitation Mistakes in Prayer
Introduction to the chapter on recitation mistakes in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle for when a recitation mistake invalidates prayer and identify the key criterion according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
A recitation mistake only invalidates prayer if it significantly changes the meaning — not any error.

This lesson introduces the important yet often neglected topic of mistakes in Quranic recitation during prayer. The author explains that these rulings are not arbitrary but are based on specific principles derived from the differences among Hanafi imams. The central criterion, according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, is whether the mistake substantially alters the meaning of the recited verse.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the importance of the topic
The author considers the rulings on recitation mistakes extremely important, yet people are heedless. Understanding this topic is essential for correct prayer.
2
Understand that rulings are rule-based
Contrary to common belief, recitation mistakes are governed by a principle (qa'ida), not arbitrary rules. The text emphasizes that it has a basis in scholarly differences.
3
Apply the principle of meaning change
For Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, the sole criterion is whether the mistake causes a significant change in meaning. If meaning changes greatly, prayer is invalid (fasid); otherwise, it remains valid.
This applies regardless of whether the mistaken word exists in the Quran or not.

Source Text

باب زلة القارى (۵۴۹) قال المحشى لما رأيت مسائل زلة القارى من اهم ما يجب العلم بها و الناس عنها غافلون ووجدت ما في الطحطاوي على المراقي اوفى ما في هذا البحث الحقة بهذا الكتاب مراعاة لمن سلک طریق الهدی و اجتنب سبل الهوى ليكون واقيا لى من النيران ووسيلة الى الجنان ورجحانا في الميزانى عند خفة الميزان و عليه التكلان قال تکمیل [1] زلة القارى من اهم المسائل و هي مبنية على قواعد ناشئة من الاختلافات لا كما توهم انه ليس له الـقـاعدة تبنى عليها .. [۲] فالاصل فيها عند الامام و محمد رحمهما الله تعالى تغير المعنى تغيرا قرآت کی غلطیاں نوٹ : فقہ کی مروج کتابوں میں قرآت کے بارے میں مسئلہ لکھا ہوا نہیں ہے، صرف نور الایضاح کے حاشیہ میں طحطاوی کے حوالے سے کچھ مسئلے ہیں، میں نے چاہا کہ اس کی پوری وضاحت کر دی جائے تاکہ طلبہ کو کام آئے ۔ میر الدین قاسمی غفرلہ (۵۴۹) محشی علیہ الرحمۃ فرماتے ہیں کہ قرآت کی غلطیوں کے مسائل بہت اہم ہیں جنکو جانا چاہئے ، اور لوگ ان سے غافل ہیں ، مراقی الفلاح پر جو طحطاوی ہے اس کو دیکھا کہ اس بحث کے بارے میں بہت کافی ہے، اس لئے اس کو اس کتاب کے ساتھ ملا دیا، جو ہدایت کے راستے پر چلنا چاہتے ہیں انکی رعایت کرتے ہوئے ، اور خواہش کے راستے سے پر ہیز کیا تا کہ آگ سے بچانے والے ہو جائے اور جنت کا وسیلہ بن جائے ، اور میزان کے ہلکا ہوتے وقت بھاری ہونے کا ذریعہ بنے ، اور اللہ تعالی ہی پر بھروسہ ہے۔ ترجمه : [۱] زلة القاری ( یعنی قرآت کرنے والے کی غلطیوں) کے احکام اہم مسائل میں سے ہیں ان کا دارمدار کچھ قاعدوں پر ہے جو علماء کے اختلاف سے پیدا ہوا ہے، ایسا نہیں ہے جیسا کہ لوگ گمان کرتے ہیں کہ قرآت میں غلطی کے لئے کوئی قاعدہ نہیں ہے تشریح : قرآت میں غلطیوں کا مسئلہ اہم ہے، اور اس کا مدار کچھ قاعدوں پر ہے۔ علماء کے درمیان اختلاف ہوا ہے،اس لئے دونوں کے قاعدے الگ الگ ہو گئے ۔ ترجمه [۲] اس میں امام ابوحنیفہ اور امام محمد کا اصول یہ ہے کہ معنی بہت بدل جائے تو نماز فاسد ہوگی ورنہ نہیں ، چاہے وہ لفظ قرآن میں موجود و یا نہ ہو۔ تشریح : امام ابوحنیفہ اور امام محمد کا اصول یہ ہے کہ لفظ کے تبدیل سے یا قرآت کی تبدیلی سے، یا اعراب کی تبدیل سے معنی بہت بدل گیا تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی ، اور معنی نہیں بدلا تو نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی ، چاہے وہ لفظ قرآن میں ہو یا نہ ہو۔ یہ اختلاف اس
Chapter of the Mistake of the Reciter. (549) The commentator said: Since I saw that the issues of the mistake of the reciter are among the most important things that must be known, and people are heedless of them, and I found that what is in al-Tahtawi on al-Maraqi is sufficient in this research, I attached it to this book out of consideration for those who follow the path of guidance and avoid the paths of desire, so that it may be a protector for me from the Fire and a means to Paradise, and a weight in the scales when the scale is light, and upon Him is reliance. He said: Completion. [1] The mistake of the reciter is among the important issues, and it is based on rules arising from differences, not as some imagine that it has no rule to build upon. [2] The principle regarding it with Imam and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) is that the change of meaning is a significant change. Note about mistakes in recitation: In popular fiqh books, there is no ruling written about recitation; only in the margin of Nur al-Idah, with reference to al-Tahtawi, there are some rulings. I desired to explain it fully so that it may benefit students. Mir al-Din al-Qasimi, may Allah forgive him. (549) The commentator, may Allah have mercy on him, says that the issues of mistakes in recitation are very important and must be known, and people are heedless of them. He looked at al-Tahtawi on al-Maraqi and found it sufficient regarding this discussion, so he added it to this book out of consideration for those who want to follow the path of guidance, and to avoid the path of desire, so that it may be a protector from the Fire and a means to Paradise, and a cause for weight in the scale when the scale is light, and trust is in Allah Almighty. Translation: [1] The rulings of the mistake of the reciter (i.e., mistakes of the one reciting) are among the important issues. Their basis is on certain rules that arise from the differences of scholars. It is not as people imagine that there is no rule for mistakes in recitation. Explanation: The issue of mistakes in recitation is important, and its basis is on some rules. There is disagreement among scholars, so their rules become separate. Translation [2] In this, the principle of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad is that if the meaning changes greatly, the prayer becomes invalid, otherwise not, whether the word exists in the Quran or not. Explanation: The principle of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad is that due to change of word or change of recitation or change of vowels, if the meaning changes greatly, the prayer becomes invalid; if the meaning does not change, the prayer does not become invalid, whether the word exists in the Quran or not. This difference is...
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage serves as an introduction to a new chapter on 'Mistakes of the Reciter' (Zallah al-Qari) during prayer. The commentator (al-Muhashi) explains his motivation for including this topic: he observed that these issues are critically important yet widely neglected. He found the most comprehensive treatment in al-Tahtawi's commentary on al-Maraqi al-Falah, so he appended it to this book. The chapter opens by establishing that the rulings on recitation mistakes are not arbitrary but are governed by specific principles derived from the differences among scholars (i.e., between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on one side and Abu Yusuf on the other, though Abu Yusuf is not mentioned here). The first principle stated is that according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, the decisive factor is the extent of change in meaning: if the mistake causes a significant change in meaning, the prayer becomes invalid (fasid); if the meaning remains unchanged, the prayer remains valid. This applies regardless of whether the mistaken word exists in the Quran or not. The passage emphasizes that this field has its own rules, contrary to the common misconception that it is rule-less. The Urdu commentary further elaborates that the principle considers changes in letters, words, or vowel markings.

Key Terms
زلة القارى (zallah al-qari): Mistakes made by the reciter (qari) during Quranic recitation in prayer, especially errors that change letters, words, or meanings.
تغير المعنى (taghayyur al-ma'na): Change of meaning; the criterion for whether a recitation mistake invalidates prayer according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, what determines whether a mistake in recitation invalidates the prayer?
A) Whether the mistake is in a letter or a word.
B) Whether the mistaken word exists in the Quran.
C) Whether the mistake causes a significant change in meaning.
D) Whether the mistake is made intentionally or forgetfully.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's principle for recitation mistakes: a mistake only invalidates prayer if it significantly changes the meaning of the recited verse.

The Two Principles of Zallat al-Qari
Intra-Hanafi disagreement on nullifying recitation errors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on recitation mistakes and apply each to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa & Muhammad: meaning change matters; Abu Yusuf: word existence in Quran decides.

Recitation mistakes in prayer are common, but their effect on validity is governed by clear Hanafi principles. This lesson explains the core disagreement between the founding imams on what constitutes a nullifying error.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Understand that the issue is whether a recitation mistake (zallat al-qari) during salah invalidates the prayer.
2
State the principle of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
Their criterion is a substantial change in meaning (taghayyur fahish), regardless of whether the resulting word exists in the Quran.
If meaning does not change substantially, prayer is valid.
3
State the principle of Abu Yusuf
His criterion is whether the mistaken word has a counterpart in the Quran. If yes, prayer is valid even if meaning changes; if no, prayer is invalid.
Diacritical marks are not considered at all.
4
Compare the two positions
Note the thamarah al-khilaf: under Abu Hanifa, a mistake like 'al-Rahman' instead of 'al-Rahim' may not invalidate if meaning is similar; under Abu Yusuf, if 'al-Rahman' is in the Quran, it is valid.
Both positions are valid ijtihad within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب زلة القارى
(۵۴۹) قال المحشى لما رأيت مسائل زلة القارى من اهم ما يجب العلم بها و الناس عنها غافلون ووجدت ما في الطحطاوي على المراقي اوفى ما في هذا البحث الحقة بهذا الكتاب مراعاة لمن سلک طریق الهدی و اجتنب سبل الهوى ليكون واقيا لى من النيران ووسيلة الى الجنان ورجحانا في الميزانى عند خفة الميزان و عليه التكلان قال تکمیل
[1] زلة القارى من اهم المسائل و هي مبنية على قواعد ناشئة من الاختلافات لا كما توهم انه ليس له الـقـاعدة تبنى عليها ..
[۲] فالاصل فيها عند الامام و محمد رحمهما الله تعالى تغير المعنى تغيرا فاحشا وعدمه للفساد و عدمه مطلقا سواء كان اللفظ موجودا في القرآن او لم يكن
[۳] و عند ابی يوسف ان كان اللفظ نظيره موجودا في القرآن لا تفسد مطلقا تغير المعنى تغيرا فاحشا او لا ، و ان لم يكن موجودا في القرآن تفسد مطلقا
[۴] ولا يعتبر الاعراب اصلا،
[۵] و محل الاختلاف في الخطاء و النسيان ، اما فى العمد فتفسد به مطلقا بالاتفاق اذا كان مما يفسد الصلوة ،
[٦] اما اذا كان ثناء فلا تفسد و لو تعمد ذالک ، افاده ابن امير الحاج

قرآت کی غلطیاں نوٹ : فقہ کی مروج کتابوں میں قرآت کے بارے میں مسئلہ لکھا ہوا نہیں ہے، صرف نور الایضاح کے حاشیہ میں طحطاوی کے حوالے سے کچھ مسئلے ہیں، میں نے چاہا کہ اس کی پوری وضاحت کر دی جائے تاکہ طلبہ کو کام آئے ۔ میر الدین قاسمی غفرلہ 
(۵۴۹) محشی علیہ الرحمۃ فرماتے ہیں کہ قرآت کی غلطیوں کے مسائل بہت اہم ہیں جنکو جانا چاہئے ، اور لوگ ان سے غافل ہیں ، مراقی الفلاح پر جو طحطاوی ہے اس کو دیکھا کہ اس بحث کے بارے میں بہت کافی ہے، اس لئے اس کو اس کتاب کے ساتھ ملا دیا، جو ہدایت کے راستے پر چلنا چاہتے ہیں انکی رعایت کرتے ہوئے ، اور خواہش کے راستے سے پر ہیز کیا تا کہ آگ سے بچانے والے ہو جائے اور جنت کا وسیلہ بن جائے ، اور میزان کے ہلکا ہوتے وقت بھاری ہونے کا ذریعہ بنے ، اور اللہ تعالی ہی پر بھروسہ ہے۔
ترجمه : [۱] زلة القاری ( یعنی قرآت کرنے والے کی غلطیوں) کے احکام اہم مسائل میں سے ہیں ان کا دارمدار کچھ قاعدوں پر ہے جو علماء کے اختلاف سے پیدا ہوا ہے، ایسا نہیں ہے جیسا کہ لوگ گمان کرتے ہیں کہ قرآت میں غلطی کے لئے کوئی قاعدہ نہیں ہے

تشریح : امام ابوحنیفہ اور امام محمد کا اصول یہ ہے کہ لفظ کے تبدیل سے یا قرآت کی تبدیلی سے، یا اعراب کی تبدیل سے معنی بہت بدل گیا تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی ، اور معنی نہیں بدلا تو نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی ، چاہے وہ لفظ قرآن میں ہو یا نہ ہو۔ یہ اختلاف اس صورت میں ہے جبکہ بھول کر غلطی ہوئی ہو، لیکن جان بوجھ کر غلطی کی ہے تو معنی کے بدلنے سے تینوں اماموں کے نزدیک نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی
ترجمه : [۳] امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک یہ ہے کہ لفظ کے مثل قرآن میں موجود ہو تو نماز بالکل فاسد نہیں ہوگی چاہے بہت معنی بدلا ہو یا نہ بدلا ہو، اور اگر قرآن میں موجود نہ ہوتو تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔
تشریح : امام ابو یوسف کا اصول یہ ہے کہ لفظ کی تبدیل کی یا اعراب کی تبدیل کی یا قرآت میں خامی آئی ، اور ایسا لفظ بن گیا کہ وہ قرآن میں ہے تو نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی ، چاہے معنی کتنا ہی بدل جائے ۔
ترجمه : [۴] اعراب کا بالکل اعتبار نہیں ہے۔
تشریح : اعراب کے اعتبار سے پیش کے بجائے زبر ہو گیا، یازیر ہو گیا تو اس کا اعتبار نہیں ہے اس سے نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی ۔
ترجمه : [۵] اختلاف کا محل غلطی اور بھول ہے، پس اگر جان کر کیا تو بالا تفاق نماز فاسد ہوگی ،اگر اس سے نماز فاسد ہوتی ہو۔
تشریح : جان کر الفاظ کی تبدیلی کی تو سب کے نزدیک نماز فاسد ہوگی ، یہ اختلاف بھول کر غلطی کرنے میں ہے۔
ترجمه : [٦] اگر حمد وثنا ہو جائے تو نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی ، ابن امیر الحاج نے یہی فرمایا۔
تشريح : الفاظ کی تبدیل سے یا اعراب کی بدلنے سے اللہ تعالی کے حمد وثنا کا معنی بن گیا تو اس سے نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ اس میں کوئی قباحت نہیں ہوئی ، علامہ ابن امیر الحاج نے یہی فرمایا۔
اصول : امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام محمد کا اصول یہ ہے کہ تبدیل سے بہت زیادہ معنی بدل جائے تو نماز فاسد ہوگی ، ورنہ نہیں
اصول امام ابو یوسف کا اصول یہ ہے کہ تبدیل کے بعد جولفظ بناہے اگر وہ قرآن میں ہے تو نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی ، چاہے کتنا ہی معنی بدلا ہو۔
Chapter: The Mistake of the Reader. (549) The glossator said: Since I saw that the issues of the reader's mistake are among the most important things that must be known, and people are heedless of them, and I found that what is in al-Tahtawi on al-Maraqi is the most comprehensive in this research, I attached it to this book, considering the one who treads the path of guidance and avoids the ways of desire, so that it may be a protection for me from the Fire and a means to Paradise, and a weight in the scale when the scale is light. And upon Him is reliance. He said: Completion. [1] The reader's mistake is among the most important issues, and it is built upon rules that arise from disagreements, not as people imagine that there is no rule on which it is built. [2] The principle with Imam Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) is the changing of the meaning excessively or not, for invalidation and non-invalidation absolutely, whether the word is found in the Quran or not. [3] And with Abu Yusuf, if the like of the word is found in the Quran, it does not invalidate absolutely, whether the meaning changes excessively or not; and if it is not found in the Quran, it invalidates absolutely. [4] And diacritical marks are not considered at all. [5] And the subject of disagreement is in error and forgetfulness; as for intentionally, it invalidates absolutely by agreement, if it is something that invalidates the prayer. [6] But if it becomes praise, it does not invalidate, even if one does it intentionally. This is what Ibn Amir al-Hajj stated. [The rest is Urdu translation and explanation of the above.]
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the ruling on mistakes made by a person reciting Quran during prayer. The author begins by emphasizing the importance of this topic and notes that it is based on rules derived from scholarly disagreements. He then outlines the positions of the Hanafi imams.

First, the principle of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad: a mistake that causes a substantial change in meaning (taghayyur fahish) invalidates the prayer, regardless of whether the resulting word exists in the Quran or not. If the meaning does not change substantially, the prayer remains valid.

Second, the principle of Imam Abu Yusuf: the criterion is whether the word (as pronounced) has a counterpart in the Quran. If a similar word exists in the Quran, the prayer is not invalidated even if the meaning changes substantially. If no such word exists, the prayer is invalidated regardless of the change in meaning. Importantly, Imam Abu Yusuf does not consider diacritical marks (i'rab) at all.

The passage clarifies that this disagreement applies only to cases of forgetfulness or error. If the reader intentionally changes the recitation, the prayer is invalidated by all three imams, provided that the change is of a type that would normally invalidate prayer. However, there is an exception: if the mistaken recitation ends up being praise of Allah (thana'), the prayer is not invalidated even if done intentionally, according to Ibn Amir al-Hajj.

The author concludes by summarizing the two principles: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad look at the degree of change in meaning; Abu Yusuf looks at the existence of the resulting word in the Quran.

Key Terms
زلة القارى (zallat al-qāri): A mistake made by a person reciting the Quran, specifically during prayer.
تغير المعنى تغيرا فاحشا (taghayyur al-ma'nā taghayyuran fāḥishan): A substantial or excessive change in the meaning of the recited verse.
الاختلاف (al-ikhtilāf): Disagreement among the Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) on the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the core criterion for invalidation according to Imam Abu Yusuf?
A) Whether the meaning changes substantially
B) Whether the mistaken word exists in the Quran
C) Whether the diacritical marks are correct
D) Whether the mistake was intentional

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school comprises two valid positions on recitation mistakes: one based on meaning change (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and one on word existence (Abu Yusuf).

Intentional Errors and the Praise Exception
Intra-Hanafi ruling on intentional recitation mistakes and the praise exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish when a recitation mistake invalidates prayer based on intent and content.

Core Idea
Intentional mistakes always invalidate, except when the result is praise of Allah.

The previous lesson covered the basic principles for forgetful mistakes. Here we address two key refinements: the effect of intentional recitation errors and the special case where the mistake results in praise (thana) of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Understand the subject of disagreement
Recall that the ikhtilaf on zallat al-qari concerns forgetful or erroneous recitation, not intentional changes.
Point [5] of the source states this explicitly.
2
State the agreed ruling for intentional mistakes
All three imams agree that if a person intentionally changes a recitation in a way that would normally invalidate the prayer, the prayer becomes invalid.
This is by consensus (bil-ittifaq).
3
Identify the exception for praise
Even if intentional, if the mistaken recitation results in praise of Allah (thana), the prayer is not invalidated according to Ibn Amir al-Hajj.
The source cites this as an additional rule, likely based on the idea that praise is beneficial.
4
Apply the exception
For example, if someone intentionally says 'subhanallah' instead of a prescribed verse, it does not invalidate because it is praise.
This exception applies only when the resulting phrase is clearly praise.

Chapter: The Mistake of the Reader. (549) The glossator said: Since I saw that the issues of the reader's mistake are among the most important things that must be known, and people are heedless of them, and I found that what is in al-Tahtawi on al-Maraqi is the most comprehensive in this research, I attached it to this book, considering the one who treads the path of guidance and avoids the ways of desire, so that it may be a protection for me from the Fire and a means to Paradise, and a weight in the scale when the scale is light. And upon Him is reliance. He said: Completion. [1] The reader's mistake is among the most important issues, and it is built upon rules that arise from disagreements, not as people imagine that there is no rule on which it is built. [2] The principle with Imam Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) is the changing of the meaning excessively or not, for invalidation and non-invalidation absolutely, whether the word is found in the Quran or not. [3] And with Abu Yusuf, if the like of the word is found in the Quran, it does not invalidate absolutely, whether the meaning changes excessively or not; and if it is not found in the Quran, it invalidates absolutely. [4] And diacritical marks are not considered at all. [5] And the subject of disagreement is in error and forgetfulness; as for intentionally, it invalidates absolutely by agreement, if it is something that invalidates the prayer. [6] But if it becomes praise, it does not invalidate, even if one does it intentionally. This is what Ibn Amir al-Hajj stated. [The rest is Urdu translation and explanation of the above.]
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the ruling on mistakes made by a person reciting Quran during prayer. The author begins by emphasizing the importance of this topic and notes that it is based on rules derived from scholarly disagreements. He then outlines the positions of the Hanafi imams.

First, the principle of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad: a mistake that causes a substantial change in meaning (taghayyur fahish) invalidates the prayer, regardless of whether the resulting word exists in the Quran or not. If the meaning does not change substantially, the prayer remains valid.

Second, the principle of Imam Abu Yusuf: the criterion is whether the word (as pronounced) has a counterpart in the Quran. If a similar word exists in the Quran, the prayer is not invalidated even if the meaning changes substantially. If no such word exists, the prayer is invalidated regardless of the change in meaning. Importantly, Imam Abu Yusuf does not consider diacritical marks (i'rab) at all.

The passage clarifies that this disagreement applies only to cases of forgetfulness or error. If the reader intentionally changes the recitation, the prayer is invalidated by all three imams, provided that the change is of a type that would normally invalidate prayer. However, there is an exception: if the mistaken recitation ends up being praise of Allah (thana'), the prayer is not invalidated even if done intentionally, according to Ibn Amir al-Hajj.

The author concludes by summarizing the two principles: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad look at the degree of change in meaning; Abu Yusuf looks at the existence of the resulting word in the Quran.

Key Terms
العمد (al-‘amd): Intentional action; in this context, deliberately changing the recitation.
الثناء (al-thanā’): Praise, especially of Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does an intentional recitation mistake NOT invalidate the prayer?
A) Never
B) When the mistake is forgetful
C) When the resulting phrase is praise
D) When the word exists in the Quran

Key Takeaway
Intentional recitation mistakes in prayer invalidate by consensus unless the resulting phrase is praise of Allah.

Ruling on I'rāb Errors That Do Not Change Meaning
States the ruling that i'rāb errors without meaning change do not invalidate prayer by consensus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on i'rāb errors that do not change meaning and apply it to identify valid and invalid recitations in prayer.

Core Idea
If the meaning stays intact, the prayer stands – consensus rules.

Reciting the Quran in prayer requires precision, but not every slip breaks it. This lesson clarifies a key Hanafi concession: errors in grammatical endings (i'rāb), tashdid, madd, or idgham are forgiven as long as the intended meaning remains unchanged. This is a matter of scholarly consensus (ijma').

Guided Path
1
Categorize the error type
Identify the specific i'rāb error from the three pairs: tashdid/takhfif (doubling/lightening), madd/qasr (long/short vowel), idgham/fakk (assimilation/separation).
These are the examples from the passage; other similar errors are covered by analogy.
2
Assess semantic change
Determine if the error alters the intended meaning of the recited verse. If the meaning remains the same despite the grammatical slip, the error is excused.
The test is meaning preservation, not grammatical correctness.
3
Apply the consensus ruling
If the meaning is unchanged, the prayer is valid (sahih) by Hanafi consensus. If the meaning changes, the prayer is invalidated.
This ruling is sourced from al-Mudmarat and agreed upon within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب زلة القارى و في هذا الفصل مسائل [6] الاولى ) الخطاء في الاعراب و يدخل فيه تخفيف المشدد و عكسه ، و قصر الممدود و عکسه، و فك الـمـدغـم و عكسه ، فان لم يتغير به المعنى لا تفسد به صلوته بالاجماع كما في المضمرات
Chapter of the Reciter's Slip. And in this chapter are issues. [6] The first: Error in i'rāb, and it includes: lightening a doubled letter and its opposite, shortening a long vowel and its opposite, and separating an assimilated letter and its opposite. If it does not change the meaning, his prayer is not invalidated by consensus, as in al-Mudmarat.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the chapter on errors made by a reciter in prayer. The author, Thamaratun Najah, begins by listing six types of i'rāb errors: reversing tashdid (doubling) and takhfif (lightening), reversing madd (lengthening) and qasr (shortening), and reversing idgham (assimilation) and fakk al-idgham (separation). The key principle is that if the meaning does not change due to the error, the prayer remains valid by unanimous consensus (ijma'). This is a straightforward rule: as long as the intended meaning is preserved, the prayer is not invalidated. The source cited is al-Mudmarat, a Hanafi fiqh work.

Key Terms
زلة القارى (zallat al-qāri'): A mistake made by a reciter during the recitation of Qur'an in prayer.
الخطاء في الاعراب (al-khaṭa' fī al-i'rāb): Error in the grammatical inflection (case endings) of words in Qur'anic recitation.
الاجماع (al-ijmā'): Consensus of scholars as a source of legal authority. Here it refers to agreement among Hanafi jurists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does an i'rāb error NOT invalidate the prayer?
A) When it is made intentionally
B) When it does not change the meaning
C) When it changes the meaning slightly
D) When it involves a long vowel

Key Takeaway
An i'rāb error in recitation does not invalidate the prayer as long as the meaning remains unchanged; this is established by Hanafi consensus.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on I'rāb Errors Changing Meaning
Intra-Hanafi dispute on i'rāb errors in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi positions on i'rāb errors that change meaning, identify the relied-upon fatwa, and apply the principle of raf' al-ḥaraj.

Core Idea
I'rāb errors in prayer are excused for common people because hardship is removed.

This passage presents a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding the effect of grammatical errors (i'rāb) in Qur'anic recitation during prayer when the meaning changes. The two positions – invalidation by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and validity by Abu Yusuf – are contrasted, and the reasoning of the later scholars who preferred Abu Yusuf's view is explained, centred on the principle of removing hardship (raf' al-ḥaraj).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
Determine what act is being discussed (i'rāb error in prayer) and what the dispute is (whether it invalidates when meaning changes).
The example is reciting 'wa idh ibtalā Ibrāhīma rabbuhu' with wrong case endings, changing the meaning to 'Ibrāhīm tested his Lord'.
2
State the two positions
State the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad (invalid) and Abu Yusuf (valid).
The text refers to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad as 'عنها' (them two) and Abu Yusuf separately.
3
Locate the dalil for each position
Identify the reasoning behind each view. The opposing view (Abu Hanifa/Muhammad) considers the change in meaning potentially kufr. Abu Yusuf's dalil is based on the principle of removing hardship (raf' al-ḥaraj).
The later scholars unanimously agreed with Abu Yusuf because most people cannot distinguish i'rāb forms.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
Determine which position is the operative fatwa according to the later scholars and the author of al-Khulāṣah.
The mufta bihi is that prayer is valid (sahih).
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
Understand the practical difference: the prayer of a common person is not invalidated by i'rāb errors, even if the meaning changes.
The exception is if the error is intentional and changes the meaning greatly, e.g., reciting 'al-Raḥman' with nasb instead of raf' (which does not change meaning much) is allowed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۸] و اذا تغير المعنى نحو ان يقرأ : و اذا بتلى ابراهيم ربه ، برفع ابراهیم و نصب ربه ، فالصحيح عنهما الفساد [9] و عـلـى قياس قول ابي يوسف لا تفسد لانه لا يعتبر الاعراب ، و به يفتى . واجمع المتأخرون كمحمدبن مقاتل و محمد بن سلام و اسماعيل الزاهد وابى بكر سعيد البـلـخـی و الهندواني و ابن الفضل و الحلواني على ان الخطاء في الاعراب لا يفسد مطلقا و ان كان مما اعتقاده كفر لان اكثر الناس لا يميزون بين وجوه الاعراب ، و في اختيار الصواب في الاعراب ايقاع الناس في الحرج و هو مرفوع شرعا [۱۰] و على هذا مشى فى الخلاصة ، فقال : و في النوازل لا تفسد في الكل ، و به یفتی ، [1] و ينبغي ان يكون هذا فى ما اذا كان خطاء او غلطا وهو لا يعلم او تعمد ذالك مع ما لا يغير المعنى كثيرا, كنصب الرحمن، في قوله تعالى :
[8] And if the meaning changes, such as if he recites 'wa idh ibtalā Ibrāhīma rabbuhu' with Ibrāhīm in the nominative and rabbuhu in the accusative, then the correct [view] according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is invalidation. [9] And on the analogy of the saying of Abu Yusuf, it does not invalidate because he does not consider i'rāb, and that is what is given fatwa upon. And the later scholars such as Muhammad ibn Muqātil, Muhammad ibn Salām, Ismā'īl al-Zāhid, Abu Bakr Sa'īd al-Balkhī, al-Hinduwānī, Ibn al-Faḍl, and al-Ḥalwānī agreed that error in i'rāb does not invalidate at all, even if it is something whose belief would be disbelief, because most people cannot distinguish between the forms of i'rāb, and requiring correctness in i'rāb would cause people hardship, and that is removed by the Shari'ah. [10] And upon this al-Khulāṣah proceeded, for it said: 'And in al-Nawāzil, it does not invalidate in all cases, and that is what is given fatwa upon.' [1] And it should be that this applies when it is a mistake or error and he does not know, or he intentionally does that which does not change the meaning much, like [reading] 'al-Raḥman' in the accusative (nasb) in His statement (the verse continues...).
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding i'rāb errors that change the meaning of the Qur'anic text. The author first gives the example of the verse (Q. 2:124) where the correct recitation is 'wa idh ibtalā Ibrāhīma rabbuhu' with Ibrāhīm in the accusative as object and rabbuhu in the nominative as subject. If one recites it with Ibrāhīm in the nominative and rabbuhu in the accusative, the meaning changes to 'when Ibrāhīm tested his Lord,' which is potentially blasphemous. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani (referred to as 'عنهما' — from them both), the correct view is that the prayer is invalid (fāsid). However, on the basis of Abu Yusuf's principle (qiyās qawl), since he does not consider i'rāb as a condition for validity, the prayer does not become invalid. The later scholars (al-muta'akhkhirūn) including Muhammad ibn Muqātil, Muhammad ibn Salām, Ismā'īl al-Zāhid, Abu Bakr al-Balkhī, al-Hinduwānī, Ibn al-Faḍl, and al-Ḥalwānī unanimously agreed that i'rāb error does not invalidate at all, even if the changed meaning amounts to disbelief. Their reasoning (ta'līl) is that most laypeople cannot distinguish between the different i'rāb forms, and requiring correct i'rāb would impose unbearable hardship (ḥaraj), which the Shari'ah has removed. Thus, the fatwa is given on Abu Yusuf's view. The author then cites al-Khulāṣah, which states that in al-Nawāzil (a collection of later rulings), the prayer is not invalidated in all such cases, and that is the operative fatwa. Finally, the author adds a condition (yambaghī) that this ruling of non-invalidation applies when the error is unintentional or, if intentional, when it does not greatly change the meaning, e.g., reading 'al-Raḥmān' with nasb instead of raf' (which changes the i'rāb but not the core meaning). This refinement guards against intentional recitation that produces blasphemy.

Key Terms
زلة القارى (zallat al-qāri'): Mistake in recitation; here specifically i'rāb errors in prayer.
الاعراب (al-i'rāb): Grammatical inflection (case endings) of Arabic words, determining roles like subject/object.
الحرج (al-ḥaraj): Hardship or difficulty that the Shari'ah seeks to remove (raf' al-ḥaraj).
المتأخرون (al-muta'akhkhirūn): Later Hanafi scholars (e.g., Muhammad ibn Muqātil, al-Halwānī) who gave fatwa on Abu Yusuf's view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is invalid in all cases
B) The prayer is valid because most people cannot distinguish i'rāb forms
C) The prayer is invalid only if the error is intentional
D) The prayer requires repetition only if the meaning changes to kufr

Key Takeaway
An i'rāb error in prayer that changes meaning does not invalidate according to the relied-upon Hanafi fatwa, due to the principle of removing hardship.

Ruling on I'rab Errors and Similar Mistakes in Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on i'rab errors and analogical extension.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on i'rab errors and takhfif al-mushaddad in prayer, explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
I'rab errors do not invalidate prayer due to istihsan based on hardship, and the mufta bihi is Abu Yusuf's view.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah addresses a practical issue: what happens if a person makes a grammatical mistake (i'rab error) while reciting Quran in prayer? The Hanafi school has three positions from its founding imams, but the later relied-upon view grants wide leniency. We will trace the reasoning, the ikhtilaf, and how the ruling extends to other similar mistakes like omitting tashdid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
The act is reciting the Quran during prayer with an i'rab error (e.g., wrong case ending). The disputed ruling is whether this invalidates the prayer. First, note the act: it is a mistake in pronunciation/grammar, not in the content.
The passage distinguishes between unintentional and intentional errors, and between minor and major meaning changes.
2
State the positions of the Hanafi imams
Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad held that an i'rab error that changes the meaning completely invalidates prayer. Imam Abu Yusuf held that it does not invalidate at all. The passage also cites other early scholars who support absolute leniency.
The ikhtilaf is intra-Hanafi, not between madhhabs.
3
Analyze the dalil: Istihsan based on hardship
The proof (dalil) for leniency is istihsan (juristic preference): requiring i'rab correctness would cause unbearable hardship (haraj) for most people, as they do not master Arabic declensions. Sharia removes hardship, so strict qiyas (which would invalidate) is overridden.
The dalil is 'aqli (rational) based on the principle of removing hardship, supported by Quran and hadith.
4
Identify the mufta bihi and its qualification
The passage explicitly states 'al-mufta bihi qawl Abi Yusuf' – the operative view is Abu Yusuf's. However, it qualifies: if the error is intentional and changes the meaning drastically (e.g., implies disbelief), then invalidation is at least possible. For unintentional or minor changes, prayer is valid.
The qualification preserves the original imams' concern for major meaning changes.
5
Extend to analogous cases: takhfif al-mushaddad and similar
The passage extends the ruling to omitting tashdid (e.g., reading 'rabbu al-'alamin' without shaddah), making idgham apparent, etc. The later scholars say these do not invalidate absolutely, because they are analogous to i'rab errors – both involve difficulty in correct articulation.
This extension shows the school's consistency in applying the same principle of hardship across various recitation mistakes.

باب زلة القارى. البـلـخـی و الهندواني و ابن الفضل و الحلواني على ان الخطاء في الاعراب لا يفسد مطلقا و ان كان مما اعتقاده كفر لان اكثر الناس لا يميزون بين وجوه الاعراب ، و في اختيار الصواب في الاعراب ايقاع الناس في الحرج و هو مرفوع شرعا [۱۰] و على هذا مشى فى الخلاصة ، فقال : و في النوازل لا تفسد في الكل ، و به یفتی ، [1] و ينبغي ان يكون هذا فى ما اذا كان خطاء او غلطا وهو لا يعلم او تعمد ذالك مع ما لا يغير المعنى كثيرا, كنصب الرحمن، في قوله تعالى : الرحمن على العرش استوى ، اما لو تعمد مع ما يغير المعنى كثيرا او يكون اعتقاده كفرا فالفساد حينئذ اقل الاحوال ، و [۱۲] المفتی به قول ابی یوسف ، [۱۳] و اما تخفيف المشدد كما لو قرأ : ایاک نعبد ، او رب العالمين، بالتخفيف ، فقال المتاخرون لا تفسد مطلقا من غير استثناء على المختار لان ترك المد و التشديد بمنزلة الخطاء في الاعراب ، كما قال قاضی خان و هو الاصح كما في المضمرات ، و كذا نص في الذخيرة على انه الاصح كما فى ابن امير الحاج ،[۱۴] و حکم تشديد المخفف كحكم عكسه في الخلاف ، و التفصيل ، وكذا اظهار المدغم و عکسه فالكل نوع واحد كما في الحلبي .
Chapter on the Lapse of the Reader. Al-Balkhi, al-Hindwani, Ibn al-Fadl, and al-Halwani hold that an error in i'rab does not invalidate prayer absolutely, even if its belief constitutes disbelief, because most people cannot distinguish between the forms of i'rab. Requiring correctness in i'rab would put people in hardship, which is removed by Sharia. This is the view followed in al-Khulasa, where it says: 'In al-Nawazil: it does not invalidate in all cases, and this is the fatwa.' It should be that this applies when the error is a mistake and he does not know, or he does it intentionally but with what does not change the meaning much, such as reading 'al-Rahman' with nasb in the verse 'al-Rahmanu 'ala al-'arshi istawa.' But if he does it intentionally with what changes the meaning much or its belief is disbelief, then invalidation is at least the case. The mufta bihi is the saying of Abu Yusuf. As for lightening a shaddah, such as reading 'iyyaka na'budu' or 'rabbu al-'alamin' with takhfif, the later scholars said: it does not invalidate absolutely without exception according to the chosen view, because leaving madd and tashdid is like an error in i'rab, as Qadi Khan said, and it is the soundest view as in al-Mudmarat, and likewise it is stated in al-Dhakhira that it is the soundest as in Ibn Amir al-Hajj. The ruling of stressing a light letter is like the ruling of its opposite in the difference and detail. Likewise, making idgham apparent and its opposite—all are one type, as in al-Halabi.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah addresses the rulings on mistakes (zallat al-qari) in Quran recitation during prayer. The author presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether errors in i'rab (case endings) invalidate prayer. He first cites several Hanafi scholars—al-Balkhi, al-Hindwani, Ibn al-Fadl, and al-Halwani—who hold that i'rab errors never invalidate prayer, even if the resulting meaning entails disbelief. Their reasoning is that most common people cannot distinguish i'rab forms, and requiring correctness would cause unbearable hardship, which Sharia removes. This view is followed in al-Khulasa and al-Nawazil, and it is the basis for fatwa. The author then qualifies: this applies when the error is unintentional, or intentional but without significantly changing the meaning. As an example, reading 'al-Rahman' with nasb instead of raf' in 'al-Rahmanu 'ala al-'arshi istawa' (Surah Taha, 20:5) does not change the meaning much. However, if one intentionally recites with a meaning change that is major or implies disbelief, then invalidation is at least required. The mufta bihi (operative view) is that of Imam Abu Yusuf, who holds that i'rab errors do not invalidate even if meaning changes, due to general hardship. The passage then extends the ruling to lightening a shaddah (takhfif al-mushaddad), e.g., reading 'iyyaka na'budu' or 'rabbu al-'alamin' without tashdid. The later scholars state that this does not invalidate prayer absolutely, because leaving madd and tashdid is analogous to i'rab error. Qadi Khan, al-Mudmarat, al-Dhakhira, and Ibn Amir al-Hajj affirm this as the soundest view. Similarly, stressing a light letter (tashdid al-mukhaffaf) and making an idgham apparent or its opposite all follow the same ruling.

Key Terms
زلة القارى (zallat al-qāri'): A mistake or slip made by a reciter of the Quran, specifically in pronunciation or grammar during prayer.
اعراب (i'rāb): The system of grammatical case endings in Arabic that indicate the syntactic function of words.
مشدد (mushaddad): A letter with a shaddah (gemination/doubling).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) It does not invalidate prayer absolutely according to the chosen view.
D) It invalidates prayer only if the person is an imam.

Key Takeaway
I'rab errors and similar recitation mistakes (like omitting tashdid) do not invalidate prayer in the Hanafi school due to the principle of removing hardship, with the mufta bihi being Abu Yusuf's view.

Rulings on Errors in Tashdid and Idgham during Recitation in Prayer
Ruling on errors in tashdid/takhfif and idgham/izhar in prayer recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on errors in tashdid/takhfif and idgham/izhar during salah, and apply the distinction between intentional errors that change meaning and those that do not.

Core Idea
Recitation errors like tashdid and idgham do not invalidate prayer unless they change meaning to kufr.

Reciting the Quran correctly during prayer is important, but what happens when a mistake occurs? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling: minor recitation errors such as lightening a shadda or making an assimilated letter clear do not invalidate the prayer, even if done intentionally, provided they do not distort the meaning into disbelief. This lesson examines the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) from the later Hanafi scholars, tracing their reasoning and the precedent from Imam Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of recitation errors
Recognize the four categories: takhfif al-mushaddad (lightening a geminated letter), tashdid al-mukhaffaf (emphasizing a light letter), izhar al-mudgham (making an assimilated letter clear), idgham al-muzhar (assimilating a clear letter).
All are treated as analogous to i'rab errors.
2
Extract the general principle
The source states that these errors are 'like an error in i'rab' (بمنزلة الخطاء في الاعراب). This is a qiyas (analogical reasoning) that forms the dalil.
I'rab errors do not invalidate prayer unless they change meaning to kufr.
3
Determine the mufta bihi position
The later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) including Qadi Khan, al-Mudmarat, al-Dhakhira, and Ibn Amir al-Hajj adopted the view of Imam Abu Yusuf: these errors do not invalidate prayer absolutely.
This is the view relied upon for fatwa.
4
Apply the condition of meaning change
The exception: if the error is intentional and changes the meaning drastically so that the reciter believes a kufr meaning, then the prayer is invalid. Otherwise (unintentional or intentional but no major meaning change), prayer is valid.
Example: 'Al-Rahman' with fatha instead of dammah does not change meaning to kufr.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The passage implies that earlier Imams (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) may have held stricter views, but the later authorities chose Abu Yusuf's position as the operative one.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate; tarjih is based on ease (taysir).

Chapter on the Slip of the Reciter. 'Al-Rahman 'ala al-'arsh istawa.' As for if one intentionally [makes an error] which changes the meaning greatly or his belief becomes kufr, then invalidity is the least [ruling]. And [12] the mufta bihi is the statement of Abu Yusuf. [14] And the ruling of emphasizing a light letter is like the ruling of its opposite in the dispute and detail. Commentary: The author says that if one intentionally makes an error in i'rab and the meaning changes so that his belief becomes kufr, then prayer should be invalid, this is the least degree. But if one makes an error in i'rab unintentionally, or intentionally but no great change in meaning, then prayer is not invalid. He gave an example: 'Al-Rahman 'ala al-'arsh istawa' (Surah Taha, 20:5). Al-Rahman should be read with dammah because it is the subject of istawa, but if one intentionally reads with fatha, it does not greatly change the meaning, so prayer is not invalid. Commentary: Fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's statement that if one makes an error in i'rab unintentionally, or intentionally but no great change in meaning, prayer is not invalid. Translation: [13] Nevertheless, lightening a shadda like reciting 'Iyyaka na'bud' or 'Rabb al-'alamin' without tashdid: the later scholars said the chosen madhhab is that prayer is not invalid, because leaving madd and tashdid is like an error in i'rab, as Qadi Khan said, and it is correct as the author of al-Mudmarat said, and likewise al-Dhakhira stated that it is correct as Ibn Amir al-Hajj said. Commentary: If one recites a letter that should have shadda without shadda, e.g., 'Iyyaka na'bud' without shadda, or 'Rabb al-'alamin' without shadda, it is like an error in i'rab, so prayer is not invalid. Qadi Khan, al-Mudmarat, al-Dhakhira, and Ibn Amir al-Hajj said this. These are four books. Translation: (14) The ruling of reading a light letter with shadda is the same as reading a shadda letter without shadda. Likewise, making an assimilated letter clear and its opposite (making a clear letter assimilated), all these forms are one type of error. As in al-Halabi. Commentary: This issue has passed, but we bring it again as a summary: [1] A letter that was light was recited with shadda. [2] A letter that was with shadda was recited light. [3] An assimilated letter was recited clearly. [4] A clear letter was recited with assimilation. These are all like errors in i'rab. Therefore, if done unintentionally, prayer is not invalid. If done intentionally, if the meaning changes greatly, prayer is invalid; if meaning does not change greatly, prayer is not invalid. Principles: [1] A light letter read with shadda. [2] A shadda letter read light. [3] An assimilated letter read clearly. [4] A clear letter read with assimilation. These are all like errors in i'rab. So if done unintentionally, prayer is not invalid; if done intentionally and meaning changes greatly, prayer is invalid; if meaning does not change greatly, prayer is not invalid.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage deals with errors in the recitation of the Quran during prayer (salah), specifically errors related to tashdid (gemination), takhfif (lightening), idgham (assimilation), and izhar (clear pronunciation). The author first gives a general rule: if a reciter deliberately makes an error that drastically changes the meaning or leads to kufr (disbelief) in the altered meaning, the prayer is invalidated. However, if the error is unintentional, or even intentional but without a significant change in meaning, the prayer remains valid. The example given is the verse 'Al-Rahman 'ala al-'arsh istawa' – if one recites 'Al-Rahman' with fatha instead of dammah intentionally, the meaning is not greatly altered (the subject becomes ambiguous but not heretical), so the prayer is still valid. Then the passage addresses specific errors: (1) lightening a letter that should have shadda (e.g., reciting 'Iyyaka na'bud' without shadda on the 'd'), and (2) emphasizing a letter that should be light. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) view according to the later Hanafi scholars is that these errors do not invalidate the prayer, regardless of whether they are intentional or unintentional, because they are analogous to grammatical errors (i'rab) which are excused as long as the meaning does not deviate into kufr. This view is supported by Qadi Khan, al-Mudmarat, al-Dhakhira, and Ibn Amir al-Hajj. The same ruling applies to errors in idgham and izhar: making an assimilated letter clear or vice versa is treated the same way. The key principle is that these are minor recitational errors that do not affect the validity of the prayer unless they lead to a serious distortion of meaning. The passage emphasizes that the mufta bihi is the view of Imam Abu Yusuf, indicating an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf where Abu Yusuf's opinion is preferred for fatwa.

Key Terms
زلة القارى (zallat al-qari): The slip or mistake of the Quran reciter during prayer.
تخفيف المشدد (takhfif al-mushaddad): Reciting a letter with shadda (gemination) without the shadda, i.e., lightly.
تشديد المخفف (tashdid al-mukhaffaf): Reciting a letter without shadda with shadda, i.e., emphasizing a light letter.
اعراب (i'rab): Grammatical inflection (case endings) of Arabic words.
مفتی به (mufta bihi): The ruling that is relied upon for issuing fatwas, the operative position.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in this passage, what is the ruling if a person intentionally recites 'Iyyaka na'bud' without shadda on the dal (تخفيف المشدد)?
A) The prayer is invalid because he intentionally changed the recitation.
B) The prayer is valid, as this is like an error in i'rab which does not invalidate.
C) The prayer is invalid only if he is a scholar.
D) The prayer is invalid if he does it out of disrespect.

Key Takeaway
Errors in tashdid/takhfif and idgham/izhar during prayer do not invalidate the prayer unless they result in a change of meaning that implies kufr, following the mufta bihi view of Imam Abu Yusuf.

Rulings on Errors in Waqf and Ibtida' during Prayer Recitation
Ruling on stopping and starting at incorrect places during Quran recitation in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on waqf and ibtida' errors in prayer, identify the two scenarios (meaning unchanged vs changed), and apply the principle of removing hardship to explain the fatwa.

Core Idea
Errors in waqf/ibtida' do not invalidate prayer, even if meaning changes, because avoiding hardship is paramount.

This passage addresses a common concern: what if during prayer recitation you stop at the wrong place or start from the wrong place? The author explains that whether the meaning changes or not, the prayer remains valid according to the relied-upon Hanafi position, based on the principle of removing hardship. This reflects the school's emphasis on ease for the worshipper.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The act is making an error in waqf (stopping) or ibtida' (beginning) during Quran recitation in salah. Note the two sub-cases: meaning unchanged vs meaning changed.
The ruling is on validity of prayer, not on sin or reward.
2
State the ruling for each case
If meaning unchanged: consensus on non-invalidation. If meaning changed: there is disagreement, but the fatwa is non-invalidation. State the Hanafi position clearly.
The mufta bihi is non-invalidation in all cases.
3
Analyze the proof
The proof is not a textual dalil but a rational principle: requiring exact waqf/ibtida' would cause hardship (haraj) especially for common people, and hardship is removed in Islamic law. This is a form of istihsan.
The sources cited are later works: al-Dhakhira, al-Sirajiyya, al-Nisab.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some early scholars reportedly held invalidity when meaning changes, but later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) overrode that, and the fatwa follows them.
This shift illustrates the living nature of the school.

Thamarat al-Najah, Volume 1, 372. The Second Issue. Chapter on the Slip of the Reciter. [15] Regarding stopping (waqf) and beginning (ibtida') in other than their proper places. If the meaning does not change, it does not invalidate by consensus of the early and later scholars. If the meaning changes, there is disagreement, and the fatwa is on non-invalidation in every case, and it is the statement of the majority of our later scholars, because observing waqf and wasl would cause people hardship, especially the common folk, and hardship is removed, as in al-Dhakhira, al-Sirajiyya, and al-Nisab. And in it also: if one leaves out waqf in all ... (corrupted). Commentary: The second issue: about waqf. Translation: [15] If one does not stop where he should and starts from another place, then if the meaning does not change, there is consensus of the early and later scholars that prayer is not invalid. If the meaning changes, there is disagreement, but the fatwa is that prayer is not invalid. This is the statement of our general later scholars, because observing waqf and wasl would cause people hardship, especially the common folk, and this type of hardship is not present in Islamic law. It is recorded in al-Dhakhira, al-Sirajiyya, and al-Nisab. In al-Nisab, it is also stated that if one leaves out waqf in the entire Quran, prayer is not invalid according to our scholars. Commentary: Where one should stop, he did not stop; or he started from a place where he should not have started. If the meaning does not change, then by consensus prayer is not invalid. If the meaning changes, still the fatwa is that prayer is not invalid, because imposing the condition of observing waqf and wasl would cause hardship for the common folk, and this is not in the Shari'ah. It is written in al-Dhakhira, al-Sirajiyya, and al-Nisab. Rather, in al-Nisab, it is written that if one leaves out waqf in the entire Quran, prayer is still not invalid.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage discusses errors related to waqf (stopping) and ibtida' (beginning) during Quran recitation in prayer. The author states that if a person stops at an incorrect place or begins recitation from a wrong place, and this does not change the meaning, there is unanimous consensus (ijma') among both early and later scholars that the prayer is not invalidated. If the meaning does change due to such an error, there is scholarly disagreement. However, the fatwa (operative ruling) according to the majority of later Hanafi scholars is that the prayer remains valid even if the meaning changes. The reason given is that requiring people to observe precise rules of waqf and wasl (connection) would cause hardship (haraj), especially for common people, and Islamic law is based on removing hardship. The passage cites al-Dhakhira, al-Sirajiyya, and al-Nisab as sources for this ruling, and even states that if one completely abandons proper waqf throughout the entire Quran, the prayer is still not invalid. This reflects the Hanafi principle of istihsan (juristic preference) based on ease and avoiding difficulty.

Key Terms
وقف (waqf): Stopping during Quran recitation, typically at the end of an ayat or at a permissible pause.
ابتداء (ibtida'): Beginning recitation, especially after a stop, from a particular point in the Quran.
حرج (haraj): Hardship, difficulty, or restriction.
متاخرون (muta'akhkhirin): Later Hanafi scholars, typically from the 6th century AH onwards.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The prayer is invalid.
B) The prayer is valid, but the person should repeat it if possible.
C) The prayer remains valid in all cases.
D) The prayer is valid only if the error was unintentional.

Key Takeaway
Errors in waqf and ibtida' during prayer do not invalidate the prayer, even if the meaning changes, because Islamic law removes hardship.

Ruling on Improper Waqf and Ibtida' in Prayer
Ruling on waqf/ibtida' with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on improper waqf/ibtida' in prayer, distinguish between cases where meaning changes or not, and explain the evidence based on the principle of removing hardship (haraj).

Core Idea
Improper stopping in recitation does not invalidate prayer, even if meaning changes, due to the Shari'ah's principle of removing hardship.

This lesson covers the second issue in the chapter on the reciter's mistake (zallat al-qari). It addresses a common practical concern: what if a person pauses or starts recitation at the wrong place during prayer, potentially altering the meaning? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on the overarching principle of removing difficulty (haraj). We will examine the two scenarios and the evidence for the lenient position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act of stopping (waqf) or beginning (ibtida') at an incorrect place during Quran recitation in prayer. The ruling is that the prayer remains valid (sahih).
This is the outcome regardless of whether meaning changes.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
First, if the meaning does not change, there is consensus (ijma') among early and later scholars that prayer is not invalidated. Second, if the meaning changes, there is disagreement among earlier scholars, but the fatwa (mufta bihi) from later scholars is that prayer is still not invalidated.
The text emphasizes that the consensus covers the first case; ikhtilaf exists only in the second.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is rational (dalil aqli): requiring precise waqf and wasl would cause hardship (haraj) for people, especially commoners. The Shari'ah principle 'difficulty is removed' (al-haraj murafi') is cited, supported by references to later Hanafi works (al-Dhakhira, al-Sirajiyya, al-Nisab).
No specific Quran or hadith verse is quoted; it is a rule-based inference.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and tarjih
The operative ruling for fatwa is that prayer is not invalidated in any case, even when meaning changes. The later Hanafi authorities (mutakhkhirin) gave tarjih to this view over the stricter earlier positions, based on the removal of hardship.
This ruling applies to unintentional mistakes; intentional alteration may carry different consequences.

The second issue: Chapter of the Reciter's Mistake. [15] Regarding stopping and beginning in other than their proper places: if the meaning does not change, the prayer is not invalidated, by consensus of the early and later scholars. If the meaning changes, there is disagreement, and the fatwa is that the prayer is not invalidated in any case. This is the view of the majority of our later scholars, because observing proper stopping and joining would cause difficulty (haraj) for people, especially the common people, and difficulty is removed, as mentioned in al-Dhakhira, al-Sirajiyya, and al-Nisab. Second issue: Regarding waqf. Translation: [15] He did not stop where he should have and started from elsewhere. If the meaning does not change, there is consensus of early and later scholars that the prayer is not invalidated. If the meaning changes, there is disagreement, but the fatwa is that the prayer is not invalidated. This is the view of our later scholars, because requiring proper waqf and wasl would cause difficulty for people, especially the commoners, and such difficulty is not present in Islamic law. It is recorded in al-Dhakhira, al-Sirajiyya, and al-Nisab. In al-Nisab, it states that even if one leaves off waqf in the entire Quran, the prayer is not invalidated according to our scholars. If meaning changes, the fatwa is still that prayer is not invalidated, because requiring such precision would cause difficulty for the common people, which is not in the Shari'a. This is written in al-Dhakhira, al-Sirajiyya, and al-Nisab. Rather, in al-Nisab, it says that even if one leaves off waqf in the entire Quran, prayer is not invalidated.

Commentary
This passage presents the second mas'alah of the chapter on mistakes of the reciter (zallat al-qari). It deals with stopping (waqf) and beginning (ibtida') in incorrect places during Quran recitation in prayer. The ruling distinguishes two scenarios: first, if the meaning does not change, there is consensus that the prayer remains valid. Second, if the meaning does change, there is disagreement among earlier scholars, but the relied-upon fatwa (mufta bihi) from the later Hanafi scholars (mutakhkhirin) is that the prayer is still not invalidated. The justification is the principle of haraj (difficulty): requiring precise waqf and wasl would impose hardship, especially on common people, and the Shari'a removes such hardship. The text cites authoritative later Hanafi works such as al-Dhakhira, al-Sirajiyya, and al-Nisab, and even states that if one leaves off proper waqf throughout the entire Quran, the prayer remains valid. Note that this ruling applies to unintentional mistakes; intentional mistakes may have different consequences.

Key Terms
زلة القارى (zallat al-qari): Mistakes made by a reciter of the Quran, specifically in this chapter regarding errors that affect the validity of prayer.
وقف (waqf): The act of stopping (pausing) during Quran recitation, usually at the end of a verse or at appropriate points.
حرج (haraj): Difficulty or hardship that Islamic law seeks to remove, used here as a principle to justify leniency.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa: improper waqf/ibtida' does not invalidate prayer, even if meaning changes, because the Shari'ah removes hardship.

Ruling on Cutting a Word During Recitation
Ruling when a reciter stops mid-word then continues

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on stopping mid-word during salah recitation and explain the rationale of darurah and umum al-balwa.

Core Idea
Cutting a word mid-recitation does not invalidate prayer due to necessity and widespread prevalence.

Have you ever been reciting a verse in salah and had to stop mid-word because you ran out of breath or forgot the rest? Does this break your prayer? The Hanafi school addresses this common scenario with a clear ruling: the prayer remains valid. In this lesson, we will examine the classical text that establishes this position and understand the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is stopping at a part of a word (qat' ba'd al-kalimah) during recitation in salah, due to necessity or forgetfulness, then either completing the word later or moving to another verse. The ruling: the prayer is not invalidated (la fasad).
This applies to unintentional interruptions; intentional tampering may have a different ruling.
2
Understand the proof (istidlal)
The proof is not a direct Quranic verse or hadith but a reasoning based on two principles: necessity (darurah) – such as running out of breath – and widespread prevalence (umum al-balwa) – meaning many people face this situation, so the Shari'a does not impose hardship by invalidating prayer.
The text cites al-Dhakhira and Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi as authority.
3
Note the ikhtilaf
There is a view (attributed to some earlier scholars) that such interruption invalidates. However, the majority of Hanafi mashayikh hold the non-invalidation view.
The text declares this view as the most sound (asahh).
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative ruling for fatwa is that prayer is not invalidated by cutting a word due to necessity or forgetfulness, even if the meaning changes.
This is based on the authority of later Hanafi jurists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[12] و اما الحكم في قطع بعض الكلمة ، كما لو اراد ان يقول : الحمد لله ، فقال :ال، فوقف على اللام ، او على الحاء ، او على الميم ، او اراد ان يقرأ : والعاديات ، فقال : والعا، فوقف على العين لانقطاع نفسه او نسيان الباقى ثم تمم او انتقل الى آية اخرى ، فالذي عليه عامة المشائخ عدم الفساد مطلقا وان غير المعنى للضرورة و عموم البلوى ، كما في الذخيرة وهو الاصح كما ذكره ابو الليث

ترجمه :[12] اگر ایک کلمہ کا کوئی ٹکڑا دوسرے سے الگ کر دیا مثلاً ”الحمد للہ“ کہنے کا ارادہ تھا، مگر پہلے ہال، کہہ کر سلام پر وقف کر دیا، یا الح کہہ کر ا پر یا میم پر وقف کر دیا، یا مثلا والعادیات پڑھنا چاہتا تھا’والعا“ کہہ کر سانس ٹوٹ جانے ، یا مثلاً باقی حصہ بھول جانے کے باعث عین پر وقف کر دیا ، یا اس کو چھوڑ کر دوسری آیت شروع کر دی تو ( ضرورت اور عموم بلوی کے پیش نظر ) عام مشائخ کا مسلک یہی ہے کہ ان صورتوں میں نماز نہیں ٹوٹتی ، اگر چہ معنی میں تبدیلی ہوجاۓ ، كما في الذخیره و هو الاصح كما ذكره ابو الليث

تشریح : لفظ کے کسی حرف پر رک گیا ، سانس ٹوٹنے کی وجہ سے رکا، یا بھول جانے کی وجہ سے رک گیا ، اور باقی کو بعد میں ادا کیا، یا دوسری آیت کی طرف منتقل ہو گیا تو چاہے معنی بدل گیا ہو تب بھی عام مشائخ اسی پر ہیں کہ نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی ، کیونکہ اس میں عموم بلوی ہے، اور عام لوگ مبتلاء ہیں۔
[12] As for the ruling on cutting part of a word: for example, if one intends to say 'al-Hamdu lillah' but says 'al' and stops on the lam, or on the ha, or on the mim; or intends to recite 'wal-'adiyat' but says 'wal-'a' and stops on the 'ayn due to running out of breath or forgetting the rest, then completes it or moves to another verse. The position of the generality of the mashayikh is that it does not invalidate absolutely, even if the meaning changes, due to necessity and widespread prevalence (umum al-balwa), as in al-Dhakhira, and it is the soundest view as mentioned by Abu al-Layth. Translation: [12] If a part of a word is separated from another, e.g., intending to say 'al-Hamdu lillah' but first says 'hal' and stops on the last letter, or says 'alh' and stops on the ha or mim; or intending to recite 'wal-'adiyat' says 'wal-'a' and stops on the 'ayn due to breath breaking or forgetting the rest, then completes or moves to another verse – due to necessity and umum al-balwa, the madhhab of the general mashayikh is that in these cases the prayer does not break, even if the meaning changes, as in al-Dhakhira, and it is the soundest as mentioned by Abu al-Layth. Explanation: He stops on a letter of a word due to breath breaking or forgetting, then performs the rest later or moves to another verse. Even if the meaning changes, the general mashayikh hold that the prayer is not invalidated because of umum al-balwa (widespread involvement) and people are afflicted with this.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific type of recitation mistake: stopping mid-word (qat' ba'd al-kalimah). Examples include saying only part of 'al-Hamdu lillah' or 'wal-'adiyat' and then either finishing after a pause or moving to another verse. The general mashayikh (scholars) rule that this does not invalidate the prayer, regardless of whether the meaning changes. The justification is twofold: necessity (darurah) – such as running out of breath – and widespread prevalence (umum al-balwa), meaning many people experience this, so the Shari'a does not invalidate the prayer due to such common occurrences. The text cites al-Dhakhira and Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi as supporting this as the soundest view. Note: This applies to unintentional mistakes; intentional tampering may have different rulings.

Key Terms
قطع بعض الكلمة (qat' ba'd al-kalimah): Stopping at a part of a word rather than completing it, then later finishing or moving on.
عموم البلوى (umum al-balwa): A principle meaning the widespread prevalence of a situation, making it too difficult to avoid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason the Hanafi mashayikh rule that cutting a word mid-recitation does not invalidate the prayer?
A) Because the meaning does not change.
B) Because of necessity and widespread prevalence (darurah and umum al-balwa).
C) Because the missing part can be repeated later.
D) Because it is not a condition of prayer to recite complete words.

Key Takeaway
Cutting a word mid-recitation due to necessity or forgetfulness does not invalidate the prayer according to the majority of Hanafi scholars, due to the principles of darurah and umum al-balwa.

Substituting a Letter in Recitation: When Prayer Remains Valid
Ruling on letter substitution in Quran recitation during prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions under which substituting a letter in Quranic recitation does not invalidate the prayer, and apply them to examples.

Core Idea
A letter substitution does not break prayer if the resulting word is still in the Quran and the meaning stays the same.

When reciting the Quran in prayer, a person might accidentally replace one letter with another. Is this mistake severe enough to invalidate the prayer? In this lesson, we learn from the Hanafi school that the prayer remains valid provided two key conditions are met. The examples from the text show how even a grammatical case ending change or a near-synonym substitution can be excusable as long as the word remains within the Quranic lexicon and the intended meaning is preserved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act of Substitution
Recognize the scenario: a letter is replaced with another in a Quranic word during prayer recitation. The resulting word may be a real Quranic word (from a different part of the Quran) or may not exist in the Quran at all.
The act itself is a mistake in recitation, not a deliberate change.
2
Check the Two Conditions for Validity
Determine if the substituted word is found anywhere in the Quran (condition 1). If yes, then check if the intended meaning of the verse has changed (condition 2). If both conditions are satisfied, the prayer is valid.
The text provides examples: 'zalumun' and 'dahaha' are both Quranic words with meanings similar to the original.
3
Apply the Ruling to the Examples
For 'inna al-zalumun' instead of 'inna al-zalimin', note that 'zalumun' is a Quranic word (e.g., Surah 67:31) and the meaning 'wrongdoers' is equivalent. Hence prayer valid. For 'wa ma dahaha' instead of 'wa ma tahaha', both are Quranic words in Surah 91:6 and mean 'spread' vs 'spread out'? The meaning is similar, so prayer valid.
If a condition fails, e.g., the resulting word is not Quranic, the prayer is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسئلة الثالثة : وضع حرف موضع حرف آخر ، فان كانت الكلمة لاتخرج عن لفظ القرآن و لم يتغير به المعنى المراد لا تفسد كما لو قرأ : ان الظلمون ، بواو الرفع او قال : و الارض وما دحها ، مكان

ترجمه [17] ایک حرف کو دوسرے حرف کی جگہ رکھ دیا، پس اگر ایسا لفظ بنا کہ قرآن کے لفظ سے نہیں نکالا ، اور معنی مراد بھی نہیں بدلا تو نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی، جیسے " ان الظالمین“ کے بجائے ان الظالمون " پڑھا جائے ، وما طحاھا کے بجائے والا رض وما دحاها (آیت 6 ، سورۃ الشمس 91 ) پڑھ دے۔ تشریح : ایک حرف کی جگہ پر دوسرا حرف پڑھ دیا لیکن اس سے ایسا لفظ بن گیا کہ وہ لفظ قرآن میں موجود ہے، اور اس آیت میں
The third issue: Substituting one letter for another. If the word does not exit the wording of the Quran and the intended meaning does not change, the prayer is not invalidated. For example, if one recites 'inna al-zalumun' with a waw of rafa', or says 'wal-ard wa ma dahaha' instead of [the correct]. Translation [17]: He placed one letter in place of another; if the resulting word does not leave the wording of the Quran and the intended meaning does not change, then the prayer is not invalidated. Like reciting 'inna al-zalumun' instead of 'inna al-zalimin', or 'wal-ard wa ma dahaha' instead of 'wa ma tahaha' (verse 6, Surah 91). Explanation: He recited one letter in place of another, but the resulting word is such that it exists in the Quran (as a word), and in this verse...
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This is the third mas'alah of the chapter, dealing with substituting a letter for another during Quran recitation. The key condition is that the resulting word must still be a word that exists in the Quran (even if in a different context), and the intended meaning of the verse must not change. If both conditions are met, the prayer is not invalidated. For example, reciting 'inna al-zalumun' (with nominative case) instead of 'inna al-zalimin' (accusative) – both are Quranic words, but the meaning change is negligible. Similarly, substituting 'wa ma dahaha' for 'wa ma tahaha' – both are Quranic expressions, and the meaning (spreading vs. covering) may be similar in context. The ruling shows that minor orthographic or morphological changes that do not corrupt the overall meaning are excusable. If the word leaves the Quranic lexicon or clearly changes the meaning, the ruling would differ. The text cuts off but the principle is clear.

Key Terms
وضع حرف موضع حرف آخر (wad' harf mawdi' harf akhar): Replacing one letter with another in a word during recitation, resulting in a different word.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person recites 'inna al-zalumun' instead of 'inna al-zalimin' in prayer, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalidated because the case ending is wrong.
B) The prayer is not invalidated because both words are Quranic and the meaning is similar.
C) It invalidates only if done intentionally.
D) The prayer is invalidated unless the person corrects it immediately.

Key Takeaway
A letter substitution in Quran recitation during prayer does not invalidate if the substituted word is Quranic and the meaning remains unchanged.

Early vs Later Hanafi Scholars on Vowel Changes in Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on vowel change effect on prayer validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding vowel changes that alter meaning in prayer and identify the preferred (mufta bihi) position.

Core Idea
A vowel change reversing Quranic meaning invalidates prayer per early Hanafis; later scholars deemed it valid to avoid hardship.

This passage presents a nuanced intra-Hanafi disagreement. While early scholars ruled that a vowel change completely reversing the meaning of a Quranic verse invalidates the prayer, later scholars adopted a more lenient view, considering the prayer valid. Understanding this ikhtilaf is crucial for evaluating prayer validity in common practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the i'rab change
Locate the specific vowel change described: the verse 'Innama yakhsha Allahu min 'ibadihi al-'ulama'' is read with nasb on 'Allah' and damma on 'al-'ulama', reversing the meaning.
The change completely reverses subject and object.
2
State the early scholars' ruling and basis
The early Hanafi scholars (mutqaddimin) ruled that such a change invalidates the prayer because the meaning is entirely altered.
Their basis is the principle that altering the Quranic meaning nullifies prayer.
3
State the later scholars' ruling and basis
Later Hanafi scholars (mutakhkhirin) held that the prayer remains valid, as their view is more accommodating (ausa') to avoid hardship for common people.
They prioritize ease and avoiding unnecessary repetition.
4
Identify the mufta bihi and the principle
The text indicates that the later view is preferred. The underlying principle is raf' al-haraj (removing hardship).
This is a common feature of later Hanafi fatwa practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
به المعنى . ككسر, قواماً، مكان فتحها ، و فتح باء نعبد ، مكان ضمها ، لا تفسد ،[۲۴] و ان غير کنصب همزة العلماء، وضم هاء الجلالة من قوله تعالى, انما يخشى الله من عباده العلماء، تفسد على قول المتقدمين .[۲۵] و اختلف المتأخرون فقال ابن الفضل و ابن مقاتل و ابو جعفر و الـحـلـوانــي وابن سلام و اسماعيل الزاهدى لاتفسد ، و قول هولاء اوسع ..
That is, the meaning. Like kasr 'qawaman' instead of its fatha, and fatha of ba' of 'na'budu' instead of its damma, does not invalidate. [24] And if he changes like nasb of hamza of 'al-'ulama' and damma of the pronoun of Allah from His statement: 'Innama yakhsha Allahu min 'ibadihi al-'ulama'', it invalidates according to the early scholars. [25] And the later scholars differed: Ibn al-Fadl, Ibn Muqatil, Abu Ja'far, al-Halwani, Ibn Salam, and Isma'il al-Zahidi said it does not invalidate, and their statement is more accommodating.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between the early scholars (mutqaddimin) and later scholars (mutakhkhirin) regarding the effect of changing vowels (i'rab) that alter the meaning in Quranic recitation during prayer. The example is the verse: 'Innama yakhsha Allahu min 'ibadihi al-'ulama'' (Fatir:28). If one reads it with nasb on 'Allah' and damma on 'al-'ulama', the meaning reverses: 'Allah fears the scholars' instead of 'The scholars fear Allah'. The early scholars ruled that this invalidates the prayer because the meaning is completely changed. However, the later scholars including Ibn al-Fadl, Ibn Muqatil, Abu Ja'far, al-Halwani, Ibn Salam, and Isma'il al-Zahidi held that it does not invalidate, as their view is broader and avoids hardship for common people. The text then indicates that the later view is the more accommodating (ausa') one.

Key Terms
متقدمون (mutqaddimun): Early Hanafi scholars before the 4th century AH.
متأخرون (mutakhkhirun): Later Hanafi scholars after the early period, known for more accommodation.
إعراب (i'rab): Vowel endings of Arabic words indicating grammatical case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later Hanafi scholars (mutakhkhirin), what is the ruling if someone changes the vowels in a Quranic verse during prayer such that the meaning is reversed?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid and does not need repetition.
C) The prayer is invalid only if done intentionally.
D) The prayer requires sajdah al-sahw.

Key Takeaway
The later Hanafi scholars' position that vowel changes not invalidating prayer is preferred for ease.
