فصل ما يكره للمصلى كميه عنهما (۵۵۵) و صلوته في السراويل مع قدرته على لبس القميص (۵۵۶) ورد السلام بالاشارة والتربع بلا عذر (۵۵۷) وعقص شعره والاعتجار وهو شد الرأس بالمنديل وترك وسطها... تشريح : (۱) گردن موڑ کر دیکھنا مکروہ ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت سألت رسول الله عن الالتفات في الصلاة فقال هو اختلاس يختلسه الشيطان من صلوة العبد ۔ (بخاری شریف، باب الالتفات في الصلوۃ ص ۱۰۴ نمبر ۷۵ / ابو داؤد شریف، باب الالتفات فی الصلوۃ ص ۱۳۸ نمبر ۹۱۰) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز میں ادھر ادھر دیکھنا مکروہ ہے۔ (۲) کتے کی طرح بیٹھنا مکروہ ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن علی قال قال النبي : يا على ! لا تقع اقعاء الكلب - ابن ماجہ شریف، باب الجلوس بین السجدتین، ص ۱۲۶، نمبر ۸۹۵ / ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی کراھیة الاقعاء بین السجدتین ، ص ۶۳ نمبر ۲۸۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ کتے کی طرح نہ بیٹھے۔ (۳) سمعت انس بن مالك يقول : قال لي النبي : اذا رفعت رأسك من السجود فلا تقع كما يقعى الكلب ، ضع ألیتک بین قدمیک ، و الزق ظاهر قدمیک بالارض ( ابن ماجہ شریف، باب الحجلوس بین السجدتین ، ص ۱۳۶، نمبر ۸۹۶ ) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ نماز میں کتے کی طرح بیٹھنا مکروہ ہے۔ (۴) زمین پر ہاتھ بچھانا مکروہ ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن انس ان النبی قال : اعتدلوا في السجود و لا يفترش أحدكم ذراعيه افتراش الكلب ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب صفته السجود،ص ۱۳۸ نمبر ۸۹۷/ بخاری شریف ، باب لا یفترش ذرا عیه فی السجود، ص ۱۱۳، نمبر ۸۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سجدے میں کتے کی طرح ہاتھ نہ بچھائے۔ لغت : اقعاء: کتے کی طرح بیٹھنا سرین کو زمین پر ٹکا دے اور دونوں گھٹنے کو اونچا کر کے سینے کی طرف ملالے، اس کو اقعاء کہتے ہیں۔ ذراعیہ: دونوں باز و تشمیر : کپڑا سمیٹنا۔ کم : آستین۔ ترجمه : (۵۵۵) قمیص پہنے پر قدرت ہوتے ہوئے صرف پائجامہ سے نماز پڑھنا۔ تشریح : کپڑا نہ ہو تو مجبوری ہے ، صرف ستر ڈھانکنے کے لئے کپڑا تب بھی نماز ہو جائے گی لیکن کپڑا ہوتے ہوئے صرف پائجامہ میں نماز پڑھے اور اوپر قمیص نہ پہنے تو اور مونڈھے پر کپڑا نہ ہوتو یہ مکروہ ہے۔ وجه : (۱) آیت۔ یا بنی آدم خذو زتنتكم عند كل مسجد . ( آیت ۳۱ ، سورۃ الاعراف ۷ ) میں ہے کہ نماز کے وقت زینت کرو اور صرف پائجامہ میں نماز پڑھنازینت کے خلاف ہے اس لئے مکروہ ہو گا۔ (۲) عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله لا يصل احدكم فى الثوب الواحد ليس على منكبيه منه شيء - ابوداود شریف، باب جماع اثواب ما یصلی فیه ص ۱۰۱ نمبر ۶۲۶ ) اس حدیث میں کپڑا ہوتو مونڈھے پر بھی کپڑا ہونا چاہئے ، یعنی پیجامہ کے علاوہ قمیص بھی ہونی چاہئے (۳) عن ابي هريرة ان رسول الله سئل عن الصلاة في ثوب واحد فقال النبي أو لكلكم ثوبان ؟۔(ابوداود شریف، باب جماع اثواب ما یصلی فیہ، ص۱۰۱، نمبر ۶۲۵) مجبوری میں ایک کپڑا ہواورستر ڈھنکا ہوا ہوتو نماز جائز ہو جائے گی۔ ترجمه (۵۵۶) اشارہ سے سلام کا جواب دینا، بلا عذر چار زانو بیٹھنا تشریح : زبان سے سلام کا جواب دے گا تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی لیکن اشارے سے سلام کا جواب دے گا تو نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی لیکن مکروہ ہے۔ بغیر عذر کے پلتی مار کر بیٹھنا، جسکو چارزانو بیٹھنا کہتے ہیں ہمکروہ ہے۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن جابر بن سمرة قال كنا اذا صلينا مع رسول الله قلنا السلام عليكم ورحمة الله ، السلام عليكم ورحمة الله واشار بيده الى الجانبين فقال رسول الله علام تؤمون بــايــديـكـم كانها اذناب خیل شمس انما يكفي احدكم اى يضع يده على فخذه ثم يسلم على اخيه من على يمينه و شماله - (مسلم شریف ، باب الامر بالسكون في الصلوة والنهي عن الاشارة بيده الخ،ص۱۸۴، نمبر ۹۷۰/۴۳۱/ ابوداؤد شریف، باب رد السلام فی الصلوۃ ص ۱۴۰، نمبر (۹۲۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہاتھ کے اشارے سے بھی سلام کا جواب نہیں دینا چاہئے ۔ (۲) پلتی مر کر بیٹھنا مکروہ ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ فقال ابو حميــد الـسـاعـدى .... فاذا جلس في الركعتيـن جـلـس عـلـى رجله اليسرى و نصب اليمني واذا جلس في الركعة الآخرة قدم رجله اليسرى ونصب الاخرى وقعد على مقعدته ( بخاری شریف ، باب سنتہ الجلوس في التشهد ص ۱۴ نمبر ۸۲۸ مسلم شریف ، باب ما تجمع صفۃ الصلوة وما تفتح به ص۱۹۴ نمبر ۱۱۰/۴۹۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تشہد میں دائیں پاؤں کو کھڑا رکھنا چاہئے اور بائیں پاؤں کو بچھا کر اس پر بیٹھنا چاہئے ۔ اس لئے چار زانوں بیٹھنا مکروہ ہے۔(۳) اس اثر میں ہے۔ قال عبد الله (بن مسعود) لان اجلس على رضفين خير من ان اجلس في الصلوة متربعا (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الاقعاء فی الصلوۃ، ج ثانی، ص ۱۲۸، نمبر ۳۰۵۷) آگ پر بیٹھنا بہتر ہے پلیتی مارکر بیٹھنے سے۔ ترجمه : (۵۵۷)، مرد کو اپنے بالوں کا جوڑا باندھنا۔ (اعتبار ) رومال سے سر کو باندھے اور بیچ میں کھلا چھوڑ دے، بار بار کپڑا سمیٹنا، سدل کرنا۔ تشریح : یہ مسائل اس اصول پر ہیں کہ زینت کے خلاف ہوں تو مکروہ ہے۔ اور کپڑے کو بار بارسنبھالنا پڑے تو مکروہ ہے۔ مرد کے لئے بالوں کا جوڑا باندھنا اس کی زینت کے خلاف ہے اس لئے مکروہ ہوگا۔ اسی طرح اعتبار، یعنی رومال سر پر لیٹے اور بیچ میں کھلا رکھے یہ مرد کی زینت کے خلاف ہے اس لئے مکروہ ہے۔ نماز میں کپڑے کو بار بار سمیٹنے سے خشوع وخضوع ختم ہو جائے گا اس لئے مکروہ ہے۔ اسی طرح سدل، یعنی کپڑے کو کندھے پر رکھکر کھلا چھوڑ دینے سے رکوع اور سجدے میں اس کے گرنے کا خطرہ ہے، اس لئے اس کو بار بار سنبھالے گا جس سے خشوع و خضوع ختم ہو جائے گا اس لئے یہ بھی مکروہ ہے۔
Chapter: What is disliked for the one praying. (555) His prayer in trousers while able to wear a qamis. (556) Responding to salam by gesture and sitting cross-legged without excuse. (557) Tying his hair, and i'tijar which is wrapping the head with a handkerchief leaving its middle exposed... Commentary: (1) Turning the neck to look is disliked; for this is the hadith from Aishah... (2) Sitting like a dog is disliked... (3) I heard Anas ibn Malik say... (4) Spreading hands on the ground is disliked... Lexicon: Iq'a: sitting like a dog, placing the buttocks on the ground and raising both knees towards the chest. Dhira'ayn: both forearms. Tashmir: rolling up the garment. 'Aql: [؟]. Translation: (555) Praying only in trousers while able to wear a shirt. Commentary: If one has no cloth, it is excusable; just covering the private parts, the prayer is valid. But if one has cloth and prays only in trousers without a shirt over the upper body and shoulders, it is disliked. Evidence: (1) Verse 'O children of Adam, take your adornment at every mosque' (7:31) commands adornment during prayer; praying only in trousers contradicts adornment, hence disliked. (2) Hadith from Abu Hurairah: 'Let none of you pray in a single garment with nothing on his shoulders' (Abu Dawud 626). (3) Hadith from Abu Hurairah: 'Do each of you have two garments?' (Abu Dawud 625) - in necessity, one garment is allowed if private parts are covered. Translation (556): Responding to salam by gesture, sitting cross-legged without excuse. Commentary: If one responds with speech, the prayer becomes invalid; but with gesture, it is valid but disliked. Sitting cross-legged without excuse is also disliked. Evidence: (1) Hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah forbidding hand gestures in prayer. (2) Hadith of Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi describing proper sitting in tashahhud - right foot upright, left foot laid flat, sitting on it. (3) Athar of Ibn Mas'ud: 'To sit on hot rocks is better than sitting cross-legged in prayer.' Translation (557): For a man to tie his hair in a bun (i'tijar is to wrap the head with a handkerchief leaving the middle open), repeatedly adjusting the cloth, and sadl (letting garment hang loose). Commentary: These matters are based on the principle: anything contrary to adornment is disliked. And anything that requires repeated adjustment disrupts khushu'. Tying hair in a bun is contrary to adornment for men, hence disliked. Similarly i'tijar - leaving the middle open - is contrary to adornment, hence disliked. Repeatedly adjusting the garment in prayer disrupts khushu', hence disliked. Sadl - placing the garment on the shoulder and leaving it loose - risks falling during ruku' and sujud, requiring continuous adjustment, also disliked.
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of actions that are makruh tanzihi (disliked but not sinful) during prayer according to the Hanafi school. The text presents a series of rulings, each supported by hadith evidence. The first ruling (555) concerns praying in only trousers (sarawil) when one has a shirt (qamis) available. The Hanafi position is that it is makruh tanzihi because it contradicts the Quranic command to take adornment at every mosque (7:31) and the prophetic instruction to have cloth on both shoulders. However, if one is compelled by necessity, the prayer is valid. The second ruling (556) covers two matters: (a) responding to the salam (greeting) by gesture (isharah) instead of speech, which is makruh tanzihi; doing so with speech invalidates the prayer. (b) Sitting cross-legged (tarbu') without a valid excuse (like illness or deep prostration) is also makruh tanzihi, as the sunnah is to sit on the left foot with the right foot upright during tashahhud. The text cites hadith from Jabir ibn Samurah and Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi to prove the proper method. The third ruling (557) addresses four actions: (a) a man tying his hair in a bun ('aqd al-sha'r), (b) i'tijar (wrapping the head with a cloth leaving the middle exposed), (c) tashmir (rolling up the sleeves or repeatedly adjusting the garment), and (d) sadl (letting the garment hang loose from the shoulders without securing it). All are deemed makruh tanzihi because they either contradict the recommended adornment (for men) or break khushu' (humility and concentration) due to repeated adjustment. The author bases these on the general principle that anything contrary to the etiquette of prayer—such as excessive movement or improper attire—is disliked. The overall authority weight is from the Hanafi school's reliance on hadith and the principle of istihsan, though the text is a later commentary (Thamaratun Najah is a modern work).

Key Terms
اقعاء (iq'ā'): Sitting like a dog: placing the buttocks on the ground with knees raised upright and drawn towards the chest.
تشمر (tashmīr): Rolling up the sleeves or repeatedly adjusting the garment during prayer to keep it from falling.
سدل (sadl): Placing the garment on the shoulder and letting it hang loose without wrapping or securing it.
التفات (iltifāt): Turning the neck or looking around during prayer.
عقص (ʿaqṣ): Tying the hair in a bun or knot, specifically for men.
اعتبار (iʿtibār): Wrapping the head with a cloth leaving the middle exposed, a form of turban but incomplete.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling on responding to the salam (greeting) by gesture during prayer?
A) It invalidates the prayer (bāṭil).
B) It is permissible (mubāḥ) and recommended.
C) It is disliked (makrūh tanzīhī) but the prayer remains valid.
D) It is prohibited (ḥarām) but the prayer is still valid.

Key Takeaway
Disliked actions in prayer reduce its perfection but do not invalidate it; they should be avoided for greater khushu' and reward.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Disliked Actions: Hair and Clothing in Prayer
Rulings with hadith proofs for disliked hair and clothing actions in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five disliked actions regarding hair and clothing in prayer according to the Hanafi school, identify the hadith proofs for each, and explain the principle that any action disturbing khushu' is makruh.

Core Idea
Any action in prayer that disturbs khushu' or imitates other practices is makruh.

In this lesson, we examine a section from Thamaratun Najah on actions that are disliked (makruh) for the praying person, specifically concerning hair and clothing. The author lists five actions, each supported by authentic hadith. Understanding these rulings helps maintain the proper adab and concentration in salah.

Guided Path
1
List the five disliked actions
Identify each action from the passage: braiding hair, topknot, folding garment, sadl, and ishtimal al-samma.
These are all considered makruh tanzihi.
2
Associate each action with its hadith proof
For each action, locate the specific hadith cited. For example, the topknot prohibition comes from Abu Rafi' narrating that the Prophet forbade praying with hair twisted.
All proofs are ahad hadith, so they are zanni al-thubut.
3
Identify the common principle
The commentary states that these actions are disliked because they disturb khushu' (humility and concentration).
Repeated folding (kaff) and sadl disrupt concentration; hair tying imitates women.
4
Note the cross-madhhab perspective
The Hanafi school considers these actions makruh, while other schools may differ on some details, e.g., Shafi'is also dislike sadl but may permit neat hair binding.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is minimal in most cases.

فصل ما يكره للمصلى مكشوفا وكف ثوبه وسدله (۵۵۸) والاندراج فيه بحيث لا يخرج يديه وجعل الثوب تحت ابطه وجه : (۱) مرد کے لئے بال گوندھنے میں عورت کی مشابہت ہے اسلئے بھی مکروہ ہے۔(۲) چوٹلا مکروہ ہے اس کے لئے حدیث یہ ہے۔ رأيت أبا رافع مولى رسول الله الله .... و قال نهى رسول الله له أن يصلى الرجل و هو عاقص شعره - (ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب كف الشعر والثوب في الصلوۃ ص ۱۴۶، نمبر ۱۰۴۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مرد کے لئے سر پر جوڑا باندھ کر نماز پڑھنا مکروہ ہے۔(۳) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ أنه رأى أبا رافع مولى النبي ع مر بحسن بن صلى الله عليهما السلام و هو يصلى قائما و قد غرز ضفره فى قفاه ، فحلها أبو رافع فالتفت حسن اليه مغضباً فقال ابو رافع : أقبل على صلوتک و لا تغضب فانى سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : يقول : ذالک کفل الشيطان ، یعنی مقعد الشيطان - یعنی مغرز ضفره (ابوداود شریف، باب الرجل یصلی عاقصا شعره، ص ۱۰۴، نمبر ۱۶۴۶ ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی کف الشعر فی الصلوۃ ، ص ۸۷، نمبر ۳۸۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ چوٹلا باندھنا شیطان کا کام ہے (۴) بار بار کپڑا اسمیٹنا مکروہ ہے اس کے لئے حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال أمر النبي له أن يسجد على سبعة صلى الله أعظم ، و لا يكف ثوبه و لا شعره ( بخاری شریف ، باب لا يكف شعر ا ص ۱۱۳ نمبر ۸۸۱۵ مسلم شریف، باب أعضاء السجودو النھي عن كف الشعر والثوب ،ص ۲۰۲، نمبر ۱۰۹۵/۴۹۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ نماز میں بال کو نہ سمیٹے ، اور چوٹلا باندھنے میں بال کو سمیٹنا ہوتا ہے اسلئے یہ مکروہ ہوگا۔ (۵) سدل مکروہ ہے اس کے لئے حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ابی هریرة ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم تھی عن السدل في الصلوة وان يغطى الرجل فاه ۔ (ابوداؤد شریف، باب ما جاء فی السدل فی الصلوۃ ، ص ۱۰۳ نمبر ۶۴۳ / ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی کراہیتہ السدل فی الصلوۃ ص ۸۷، نمبر ۳۷۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سدل کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ لغت : التربع : ربع سے مشتق ہے چار زانو بیٹھنا۔ عقص الشعر : مرد بالوں کو جمع کر کے باندھے، یا چوٹی گوند ھے۔ اعتبار: عجر سے مشتق ہے ، لیٹنا، یہاں مراد ہے، کہ رومال سر کے چاروں طرف لپیٹے اور بیچ میں کھلا رکھے۔ کف الثوب : کپڑے کو بار سمیٹنا۔ سدل : کندھے پر چادر یا رومال رکھ دے، اور اس کو لپیٹے نہیں کھلا چھوڑ دے۔ ترجمه : (۵۵۸) کپڑے میں اس طرح ہاتھ داخل کرنا کہ نہ نکل سکے۔ کپڑے کو داہنی بغل سے نکال کر اس کے دونوں کنارے بائیں کندھے پر ڈالنا۔ تشریح : یہ مسئلے اس اصول پر ہیں کہ کپڑا بار بار سمیٹنے سے خشوع خضوع میں خلل آتا ہو تو مکروہ ہوگا۔ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے، نماز میں کپڑے میں اس طرح ہاتھ ڈالے کے باہر نہ نکل سکے [ اس کو عربی میں الصماء، کہتے ہیں] اس سے رکوع اور سجدے میں پریشانی ہوگی اس لئے یہ اس لئے مکروہ ہے ۔ کپڑے کو داہنی بغل میں ڈالے اور وہاں سے نکال کر بائیں کندھے پر ڈالے اس میں تھوڑا تکبر کا مظاہرہ ہوتا ہے، جوصرف حج میں ریل کے وقت مستحسن ہے باقی میں نہیں۔ وجه : (۱) صماء مکروہ ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عـن جـابـر قـال نھی رسول الله له عن الصماء و عن الاحتباء في ثوب واحد - ابوداود شریف ، باب فی لبسة الصماء، ص ۵۷۵، نمبر ۴۰۸۰) اس حدیث میں کہ لبستہ صماء نہ کرے (۲) دائیں بغل کے نیچے کپڑا ڈالے اور بائیں کندھے پر ڈالے، یہ مکروہ ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة قال صل الله نهى رسول الله له عن لبستين ان يحتبى الرجل مفضيا بفرجه الى السماء و يلبس ثوبه و احد جانبيه خارج و يلقى ثوبه على عاتقه - (ابوداود شریف، باب فی لبسته الصماء ،ص ۵۷۵، نمبر ۴۰۸۰) اس حدیث میں کہ اندراج مکروہ ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة قال نهى النبى الله ان يصلى الرجل في الثوب الواحدليس على عاتقه منه شيء ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب فی اعراء المناسب، ج اول ص ۳۰۷ نمبر ۳۵۰۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ کندھے پر کپڑا نہ ہو تو حضور نے نماز منع فرمائی ہے۔
Section on what is disliked for the praying person: (558) Exposed, and folding his garment, and letting it hang, and wrapping himself in it such that he cannot get his hands out, and placing the garment under his armpit. Explanation: (1) For a man to braid his hair resembles women, therefore it is also disliked. (2) A topknot is disliked, about which there is this hadith: I saw Abu Rafi' the freed slave of the Messenger of Allah... and he said the Messenger of Allah forbade that a man pray while his hair is twisted. (3) In this hadith: He saw Abu Rafi' the freed slave of the Prophet... pass by Hasan ibn 'Ali while he was praying standing and had braided his hair at the nape of his neck. Abu Rafi' undid it, Hasan turned to him angrily, so Abu Rafi' said, 'Turn to your prayer and do not be angry, for I heard the Messenger of Allah say: That is the seat of Satan.' (4) Repeatedly folding the garment is disliked, about which is this hadith: Ibn 'Abbas said the Prophet ordered to prostrate on seven bones and not to fold his garment or his hair. (5) Sadl (letting the cloth hang loose) is disliked, about which is this hadith: Abu Hurairah reported that the Messenger of Allah forbade sadl in prayer and that a man cover his mouth. Lexicon: al-tarbu': derived from rub', sitting cross-legged. 'Aqs al-sha'r: a man gathering and tying his hair, or plaiting it. I'tibar: derived from 'ajr, lying down; here it means wrapping a scarf around the head and leaving the middle open. Kaff al-thawb: repeatedly folding the garment. Sadl: placing a sheet or scarf on the shoulder without folding it. Translation: (558) Inserting the hands into the garment such that they cannot come out; taking the garment out from the right armpit and throwing its two ends over the left shoulder. Commentary: These issues are based on the principle that if repeatedly folding the garment disturbs humility and concentration, it is disliked. The case: inserting the hands into the garment such that they cannot come out, called 'al-samma' in Arabic, causes difficulty in bowing and prostrating, so it is disliked. Placing the garment under the right armpit and throwing it over the left shoulder involves a slight display of pride, which is only considerd good during ramal in Hajj, not otherwise. Proof: (1) Al-samma is disliked, as in this hadith: Jabir said the Messenger of Allah forbade al-samma and wrapping in a single garment. (2) Putting the garment under the right armpit and over the left shoulder is disliked, as in the hadith from Abu Hurairah: The Messenger of Allah forbade two types of clothing: wrapping such that the private parts are exposed to the sky, and wearing a garment with one side out and throwing it over the shoulder. Also, Abu Hurairah said the Prophet forbade a man to pray in a single garment with nothing on his shoulders.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage is a section on actions disliked (makruh) for the praying person, specifically regarding hair and clothing. The text lists five disliked actions with hadith proofs: (1) a man braiding his hair because it resembles women; (2) wearing a topknot (braid tied at the back), which is explicitly forbidden in hadith from Abu Rafi'; (3) repeatedly folding the garment during prayer, which disturbs khushu'; (4) sadl, letting the cloth hang loosely without folding; (5) ishtimal al-samma, wrapping oneself so that hands cannot come out, causing difficulty in bowing and prostration. The commentary explains that these rulings stem from the principle that anything disrupting humility (khushu') is disliked. The final part addresses placing the garment under the right armpit and throwing it over the left shoulder, which is disliked except during ramal (quick pace) in Hajj. All proofs are from authentic hadith sources.

Key Terms
عقص الشعر ('aqs al-sha'r): A man gathering and tying his hair, or forming a plait/topknot.
كف الثوب (kaff al-thawb): Repeatedly folding or gathering the garment during prayer.
سدل (sadl): Letting the garment hang loosely on the shoulders without folding or gathering.
الصماء (al-samma'): Wrapping the garment around the body such that the hands cannot be brought out, used for ishtimal al-samma.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Recommended (mandub)
B) Permissible (mubah)
C) Disliked (makruh)
D) Forbidden (haram)

Key Takeaway
Five actions regarding hair and clothing are makruh in Hanafi prayer: braiding hair, topknot, folding garment, sadl, and ishtimal al-samma.

Recitation in Ruku' and Sujud: Hanafi Ruling
Ruling on recitation outside qiyam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting Quran in ruku' and sujud, identify the proof, and explain why it is makruh tanzihi rather than haram.

Core Idea
Recitation is for standing; performing it in ruku' or sujud is disliked but does not invalidate prayer.

The Quran is the speech of Allah, and its recitation is a fundamental part of prayer. However, the prayer has prescribed postures, and recitation is specifically linked to standing (qiyam). The Prophet forbade recitation in ruku' and sujud, leading Hanafi scholars to rule it makruh tanzihi – disliked but not invalidating. This lesson examines the proof and the school's reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is reciting Quran while in ruku' or sujud. The Hanafi ruling is makruh tanzihi (disliked, not sinful).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith from Ali ibn Abi Talib: 'The Messenger of Allah forbade me from recitation in ruku' and sujud.' (Sahih Muslim)
This is a sahih hadith, but ahad (single-chain).
3
Classify the dalil
It is a Sunnah ahad, zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala. The prohibition (nahy) in Hanafi usul indicates karahah unless accompanied by evidence of haram.
Contrast with strong prohibitions that indicate haram.
4
Understand wajh al-dalalah
The word 'nahani' (forbade me) is a prohibition. Hanafi usul states that a prohibition without evidence of severity indicates makruh tanzihi, not haram.
The ruling is further softened by the principle that Quran is for standing; its recitation elsewhere is out of place but not invalidating.
5
Note cross-madhhab status
Shafi'is consider intentional recitation in ruku' or sujud as invalidating the prayer. Hanafis maintain the prayer is valid, though the act is disliked.
This difference impacts fatwa: a Hanafi imam who recites in ruku' does not require repetition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۵۵۹) قیام کے سوا دوسری حالت میں قرآن پڑھنا نفل میں پہلی رکعت کو دراز کرنا، پہلی رکعت سے دوسری رکعت کو تمام نمازوں میں طویل کرنا۔ تشریح : قیام کے علاوہ دوسری حالتوں میں قرآت کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ نفل میں پہلی رکعت کو اتنا لمبا کرے کہ برابری ختم ہو جائے یہ مکروہ ہے، تھوڑا بہت لمبا ہو جائے تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ تمام نمازوں میں پہلی رکعت اور دوسری رکعت برابر ہوں یا تھوڑی بہت پہلی رکعت بڑی ہو، لیکن اس کے برخلاف دوسری رکعت کو پہلی رکعت سے بھی لمبی کر لینا مکروہ ہے۔ وجه : (۱) قیام کے علاوہ میں قرآت مکروہ ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن علی بن ابی طالب قال نهانی رسول الله له عـن التـخـتـم بـالـذهـب وعـن لباس القسى و عن القرأة في الركوع و السجود و عن لباس المعصفر. (مسلم شریف ، باب النهي عن لطس الرجل الثوب المعصفر ،ص ۹۳۱، نمبر ۵۴۳۹/۲۰۷۸) (۲) دوسری پر پہلی کولمبی کرنا مکروہ ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن ابی قتادة ، عن ابيه قال : كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقرأ في الركعتين الأوليين من صلاة الظهر بفاتحة الكتاب و سورتين ، يطول في الاولى و يقصر في الثانية و يسمع الآية احيانا ، و كان يقرأ فى العصر بفاتحة الكتاب و سورتين ، و كان يطول في الاولى ، و كان يطول في الركعة الأولى من صلوة الصبح ، و يقصر في الثانية - ( بخاری شریف، باب القرآة في الظھر میں ۱۰۵، نمبر ۷۵۹ے مسلم شریف، باب القرآة فی الظهر ص ۱۸۵، نمبر ۱۰۱۲/۴۵۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پہلی رکعت کو لمبی کرتے اور دوسری رکعت کو اس سے چھوٹی کرتے۔
Translation: (559) Reciting the Quran in a state other than standing, lengthening the first rak'ah in supererogatory prayer, making the second rak'ah longer than the first in all prayers. Commentary: Recitation in states other than standing is disliked. In nafl, lengthening the first rak'ah to the point that equivalence is lost is disliked; a slight length is not harmful. In all prayers, the first and second rak'ahs should be equal, or the first slightly longer, but making the second longer than the first is disliked. Proof: (1) Recitation outside standing is disliked, as in this hadith: 'Ali ibn Abi Talib said the Messenger of Allah forbade me from wearing gold rings, wearing silk, reciting during ruku' and sujud, and wearing saffron-dyed cloth. (2) Making the first longer than the second is disliked, as in the hadith from 'Abdullah ibn Abi Qatada from his father: The Prophet used to recite in the first two rak'ahs of Zuhr with Fatiha and two surahs, lengthening the first and shortening the second, and sometimes making a verse audible; he lengthened the first rak'ah of Asr and the first rak'ah of Fajr, shortening the second.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage describes two disliked actions in prayer: (1) reciting Quran in postures other than standing (qiyam)—i.e., during ruku' or sujud—based on the hadith from 'Ali where the Prophet forbade recitation in ruku' and sujud; (2) making the first rak'ah disproportionately long in nafl prayers, or generally making the second rak'ah longer than the first. The commentary clarifies that slight differences are acceptable, but noticeable imbalance is makruh. The proof for the second point comes from the practice of the Prophet, who consistently lengthened the first rak'ah and shortened the second in both obligatory and supererogatory prayers.

Key Terms
النهي (al-nahy): Prohibition. In this lesson, the Prophet's prohibition is interpreted as indicating karahah (dislike) not hurmah (unlawfulness).
الكراهة التنزيهية (al-karahah al-tanzihiyyah): Disliked but not sinful. The prayer remains valid even if performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on reciting the Quran during ruku' (bowing)?
A) Forbidden (haram) and invalidates the prayer
B) Disliked (makruh tanzihi) but prayer remains valid
C) Permissible (mubah) and recommended
D) Only allowed in the last rak'ah

Key Takeaway
Recitation in ruku' and sujud is makruh tanzihi; the prayer remains valid and does not need repetition.

Lengthening Rak'ahs: First vs. Second
Ruling on rak'ah length in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on rak'ah length: identify when lengthening the first rak'ah is recommended, when it becomes disliked, and the ruling for making the second rak'ah longer than the first.

Core Idea
The first rak'ah should be equal or slightly longer than the second; making the second longer is disliked in all prayers.

The Prophet's practice was to lengthen the first rak'ah and shorten the second in both fard and nafl prayers. Hanafi scholars derive from this that maintaining a balance – with the first being equal or slightly longer – is recommended, while reversing this (making the second longer) becomes makruh. This lesson explores the evidence and the detailed ruling for supererogatory and obligatory prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Scenario A: Lengthening the first rak'ah in nafl prayer – slight lengthening is fine, but excessive (eliminating equality) is makruh. Scenario B: Making the second rak'ah longer than the first in any prayer is makruh.
2
Locate the dalil for scenario B
The proof is the hadith from Abdullah ibn Abi Qatada describing the Prophet's practice: he lengthened the first rak'ah and shortened the second in Zuhr, Asr, and Fajr.
This establishes the sunnah pattern.
3
Understand the prophetic practice
The Prophet consistently made the first rak'ah longer than the second. This indicates the recommended (mustahabb) practice. Deviation from it, especially reversing the pattern, is disliked (makruh).
The hadith is clear that the first is longer; the second is shorter.
4
Apply the ruling to nafl vs fard
In nafl, if one exaggerates the length of the first rak'ah to the point that equality is lost, it is also makruh. In all prayers, making the second longer is makruh, regardless of the type.
The dislikedness in scenario B is general; scenario A is specific to nafl.
5
Note the exception
A slight difference (first slightly longer) is not harmful. The ruling applies to noticeable imbalance.
The passage says 'a slight length is not harmful.'

Source Text

Disliked Actions in Prayer: Clothing, Recitation, and Movement
Listing disliked actions in prayer with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on at least three disliked actions in salah (as-samma', reciting in non-standing positions, and repeating surahs) and identify the evidence from hadith that supports each ruling.

Core Idea
Disliked actions (makruhat) in prayer do not invalidate it, but avoiding them perfects one's devotion.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah outlines several actions that, while not invalidating prayer, are considered disliked (makruh) in the Hanafi school. The author provides proofs from hadith and sayings of the Companions. Understanding these rulings helps you refine your prayer practice and avoid what the Prophet disapproved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disliked action
Pinpoint what exactly is being ruled upon, e.g., wearing as-samma', reciting in ruku', repeating surahs in fard, or smelling perfume during prayer.
Each action is listed with a number in the text.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
Determine the hukm level. In this passage, all actions are makruh tanzih (light dislike) — not invalidating but better to avoid.
The Hanafi school distinguishes makruh tanzih from makruh tahrimi; here the text implies tanzih.
3
Locate the dalil
Find the specific hadith or athar cited for each action. For example, as-samma' is supported by a hadith from Jabir; recitation in ruku' by a hadith from Ali.
The proofs are from authentic sources like Abu Dawud, Muslim, and Bukhari.
4
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the dalil proves the ruling. For instance, an explicit prohibition (nahi) indicates the action is disliked, but since the hadith is ahad (zanni), it indicates tanzih rather than tahrimi.
Hanafi usul: nahi from ahad hadith yields makruh tahrimi unless counterbalanced; here the context tilts towards tanzih.
5
Note the scope and conditions
Some actions have exceptions: repeating surahs is makruh only in fard, not nafl; skipping a surah is excused if forgotten; perfume on the body is fine, but deliberately smelling is not.
These nuances are explained in the commentary following each number.

ثمرة النجاح جلد ا
۳۸۸
فصل ما يكره للمصلى
من الفرض وقراءة سورة فوق التي قرأها وفصله بسورة بين سورتين قرأهما في ركعتين (۵۶۱) وشم طيب وترويحه بثوب او مروحة مرة او مرتين
مختصر کرتے تھے۔
ترجمه : (۵۶۰) فرض کی ایک رکعت میں مکر رسورت پڑھنا، او پر کی سورت پڑھنا، دورکعت میں دوسورتوں کے مابین ایک چھوٹی سورت کا فاصلہ کرنا۔
تشریح : فرض کی رکعت میں کئی سورتیں پڑھے گا تو رکعت لمبی ہو جائے گی، جس سے مقتدی کو تکلیف ہوگی اس لئے ایک رکعت میں کئی کئی سورتیں پڑھنا مکروہ ہے۔ قرآن کریم ترتیب کے ساتھ لکھا ہوا ہے، اس کے خلاف الٹی ترتیب سے پڑھنا خلاف ترتیب ہے اس لئے مکروہ تنزیہی ہے، مثلا پہلی رکعت میں اذا جاء نصر اللہ، پڑھے اور دوسری رکعت میں قل یا ایھا الکافرون، پڑھے یہ مکروہ ہے ۔ دو چھوٹی سورتوں کے درمیان ایک چھوٹی سورت چھوڑنے سے اس کی بے اعتنائی معلوم ہوتی ہے اور ایک قسم کی تو ہین ہے ،مثلا پہلی رکعت میں انا اعطیناک الکوثر ، پڑھے اور دوسری رکعت میں اذا جاء نصر اللہ ، پڑھے اور بیچ میں قبل یا ایھا الکافرون کو چھوڑ دے تو یہ اس کی تو ہین ہے اس لئے بغیر کسی مجبوری کے چھوڑ دینا مکروہ ہے ، ہاں یاد نہ ہو یا کوئی مجبوری ہو تو مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ یا بڑی سورت چھوڑ دے تو مکروہ نہیں ہے، کیونکہ اتنی بڑی سورت ہر کسی کو یاد نہیں ہوتی۔ وجه : (۱) مکر رسورت پڑھنا مکروہ ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابی هـريـــة ان النبي الله قال اذا صلى احدكم للناس فليخفف فان فيهم السقيم و الشيخ الكبير و ذو الحاجة ـ (ابوداود شریف ، باب تخفیف الصلاة، ص۱۲۴، نمبر ۷۹۵) (۲) یہ قول صحابی بھی ہے۔ عن ابی جعفر قال لا يقرن بين سورتين في كل ركعة _(مصنف ابن ابی شبية ، باب من كان لا تجمع بین السورتین فی رکعۃ ، ج اول ص ۳۲۴ نمبر ۳۷۰۵) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ ایک رکعت میں دوسورتیں نہیں پڑھنی چاہئے۔ ہاں نفل میں جتنی چاہے سورتیں پڑھے ۔ (۳) عن عبد الله بن ابي الهذيل قال كانوا يكرهون ان يقرأوا بعض الآية ويتركوا بعضها - (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من کره ان يقر البعض الآية ويترك بعضها ، ج سادس ص ۱۵۱، نمبر ۳۰۲۵۵) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ درمیان سے بعض آیت چھوڑ نا مکروہ ہے۔ (۴) عن شقيق قال قيل لعبد الله ان فلانا يقرأ القرآن منكوسا ، فقال عبد الله ذاك منكوس القلب ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من کره ان يقرا القرآن منكوسا ، ج سادس، ص ۱۵۵، نمبر ۳۰۲۹۸) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ قرآن الٹا پڑھنا دل کے الٹے ہونے کی دلیل ہے۔ ترجمه : (۵۶۱) خوشبو سونگھنا، کپڑے یا پنکھے سے ایک یا دو بار ہوا کرنا۔ تشریح : کپڑے یا بدن میں خوشبو لگی ہوئی ہو اور اسکی بوناک میں آ رہی ہو یہ مکروہ نہیں ہے لیکن قصدا انگلی کو ناک میں لیجا کر سونگھنا عمل کثیر کا خطرہ ہے اس لئے یہ مکروہ ہے۔ کپڑے یا پنکھے سے نماز میں ہوا کرنا عمل کثیر کا خطرہ ہے، اور یہ محسوس ہوتا ہے کہ یہ کپڑ ۔
Chapter on What Is Disliked for the One Praying. (559) The right [side] and placing its sides on his left shoulder. (560) And recitation in other than standing, and lengthening the first rak'ah in supererogatory [prayer], and making the second longer than the first in all prayers. (561) And repeating a surah in one rak'ah it appears, that only in Hajj during the [?] time is recommended, otherwise not. Proof: (1) As-Samma' (a garment covering one side) is disliked. For this is the hadith: from Jabir who said: The Messenger of Allah forbade as-samma' and wrapping oneself in a single garment. (Abu Dawud, chapter on the garment as-samma', p.575, no.4080). In this hadith [it says] do not wear as-samma'. (2) Placing the cloth under the right armpit and on the left shoulder is disliked. Its proof is the hadith: from Abu Huraira who said: The Messenger of Allah forbade two ways of dressing: that a man should squat exposing his private parts to the sky, and that he should wear his garment with one side outside and throw his garment over his shoulder. (Abu Dawud, chapter on the garment as-samma', p.575, no.4080). In this hadith [it says] that [such] wrapping is disliked. From Abu Huraira who said: The Prophet forbade a man to pray in a single garment with nothing on his shoulders. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaibah, chapter on baring the shoulder, vol.1 p.307 no.3509). In this hadith [it says] that if there is no cloth on the shoulder, the Prophet prohibited prayer. Translation of (559): Reciting Quran in other than standing, lengthening the first rak'ah in supererogatory prayer, making the second longer than the first in all prayers. Commentary: Reciting in other than standing is makruh. In nafl, if one makes the first rak'ah so long that equality is lost, that is makruh; if slightly longer, no harm. In all prayers, the first and second rak'ahs should be equal or the first slightly longer; making the second longer than the first is makruh. Proof: (1) Reciting other than standing is makruh. For this is the hadith: from Ali ibn Abi Talib who said: The Messenger of Allah forbade me from wearing gold rings, from wearing qassi (a type of silk), from reciting in ruku' and sujud, and from wearing safflower-dyed cloth. (Muslim, chapter on prohibition of the man wearing safflower-dyed cloth, p.931, no.5439/2078). (2) Making the second longer than the first is makruh. For this is the hadith: from Abdullah ibn Abi Qatada from his father who said: The Messenger of Allah used to recite in the first two rak'ahs of Zuhr prayer the Fatiha and two surahs, making the first long and the second short, and sometimes making the verse audible. And he used to recite in 'Asr the Fatiha and two surahs, making the first long. And he used to make the first rak'ah of Fajr long and the second short. (Bukhari, chapter on recitation in Zuhr, p.105, no.759; Muslim, chapter on recitation in Zuhr, p.185, no.1012/451). In this hadith [it says] that he would lengthen the first rak'ah and shorten the second. From the [page break] Section on makruh for the worshipper: from fard, and reading a surah above the one he read, and separating between two surahs that he read in two rak'ahs with a surah (561), and smelling perfume and fanning it with cloth or fan once or twice. They used to shorten. Translation of (560): In fard, repeating a surah in one rak'ah, reading a surah above the one read, separating between two surahs in two rak'ahs with a surah. Commentary: If one reads several surahs in one rak'ah of fard, the rak'ah becomes long, causing hardship to the followers, so it is makruh. The Quran is written in order; reading in reverse order is against order, so it is makruh tanzihi, e.g., in the first rak'ah read 'Idha ja'a nasru Llah' and in the second read 'Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun' is makruh. Skipping a small surah between two small surahs shows disregard and a kind of disrespect, e.g., in first rak'ah read 'Inna a'tayna al-kawthar' and in second 'Idha ja'a nasru Llah' and leave out 'Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun' in between is makruh unless one forgets or has an excuse. If one skips a large surah, it is not makruh because not everyone knows it. Proof: (1) Repeating a surah is makruh. For this is the hadith: from Abu Huraira that the Prophet said: When one of you leads the people in prayer, let him lighten it, for among them are the sick, the old, and the one with need. (Abu Dawud, chapter on lightening prayer, p.124, no.795). (2) There is also the saying of a companion: from Abu Ja'far who said: Do not combine two surahs in each rak'ah. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaibah, chapter on those who would not combine two surahs in one rak'ah, vol.1 p.324 no.3705). In this companion's saying [it says] one should not recite two surahs in one rak'ah. But in nafl, recite as many as you wish. (3) From Abdullah ibn Abi al-Hudhayl who said: They used to dislike reciting part of a verse and leaving part of it. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaibah, chapter on those who disliked reciting part of a verse and leaving part, vol.6 p.151 no.30255). In this tabi'i's saying [it says] skipping part of a verse in the middle is makruh. (4) From Shaqiq who said: It was said to Abdullah: So-and-so recites the Quran inverted. Abdullah said: That one has an inverted heart. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaibah, chapter on those who disliked reading the Quran inverted, vol.6 p.155 no.30298). In this companion's saying [it says] reading the Quran backwards is a sign of an inverted heart. Translation of (561): Smelling perfume, and fanning oneself with cloth or fan once or twice. Commentary: If perfume is on one's body or clothes and its scent reaches him, it is not makruh. However, deliberately bringing the finger to the nose to smell involves excessive movement (amal kathir), so it is makruh. Fanning with cloth or fan during prayer involves risk of excessive movement, and it is perceived that the cloth...

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of rulings on disliked actions (makruhat) in prayer, presented with proofs from hadith and sayings of the Companions. The text first lists three numbered points: (559) regarding a specific clothing style where one places the cloth on the opposite shoulder, (560) covering recitation while not standing and lengthening the first rak'ah in nafl or making the second longer than the first in any prayer, and (561) concerning repeating a surah in one rak'ah, reading surahs out of order, skipping a surah between two surahs, and smelling perfume or fanning. The author then provides detailed explanations for each. For (559), he explains that the disliked action is called 'samma''—wearing a garment that exposes one side—and supports it with a hadith from Jabir. He also includes two other related clothing prohibitions: placing the cloth under the right armpit and on the left shoulder (which exposes the right arm) and praying with nothing on the shoulders. All these are makruh because they resemble the dress of non-believers or exhibit carelessness. For (560), despite the translation being incorrectly labeled as (559), the commentary clarifies that reciting in positions other than standing (e.g., in ruku' or sujud) is makruh, and the Prophet forbade it. Lengthening the first rak'ah in nafl is makruh only if it excessively outweighs the second; slight difference is fine. In all prayers, making the second rak'ah longer than the first is makruh, as the Prophet's practice was to make the first longer. For (561), the text discusses several matters: repeating a surah in one rak'ah of fard is makruh because it lengthens the prayer and burdens the congregation; reading surahs in reverse order (e.g., a later surah in the first rak'ah and an earlier one in the second) is makruh tanzihi (disliked but not sinful) because it violates the Quranic order; skipping a small surah between two surahs is also makruh as it shows disrespect. However, if one forgets or has an excuse, it is not makruh. Regarding perfume and fanning, the text notes that merely having perfume on is not disliked, but deliberately smelling it or fanning oneself with cloth or fan involves excessive movement (amal kathir) and thus is makruh. The proofs for (561) include hadith about lightening prayer for the congregation, sayings of Companions and Successors against combining surahs, and a statement that reading the Quran backwards indicates a corrupt heart. Throughout, the commentary follows the author's order, addressing each ruling with its specific evidence and qualification.

Key Terms
الصماء (as-samma'): A garment that covers one side of the body, leaving the other side bare
مكروه (makruh): An action that is disliked and better to avoid; usually refers to makruh tanzih (light dislike) in this context
مكرر السورة (tikrar as-surah): Repeating the same surah or reciting multiple surahs in one rak'ah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on reciting a surah in ruku' or sujud?
A) Haram and invalidates prayer
B) Makruh (disliked) but prayer remains valid
C) Sunnah and recommended
D) Mubah (permissible) with no issue

Key Takeaway
Disliked actions (makruhat) in prayer are not invalidating, but avoiding them demonstrates adherence to the Sunnah and respect for the prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Ruling on Reciting Multiple Surahs in Fard Prayer
Ruling with proof on three disliked acts in fard prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting multiple surahs in one rak'ah, reciting surahs out of order, and interposing surahs in fard prayer, and identify the exceptions.

Core Idea
Reciting multiple surahs in a fard rak'ah is makruh tanzihi to avoid hardship and disrespect to Qur'anic order.

In this lesson, we examine three related disliked actions in fard prayer: reciting multiple surahs in one rak'ah, reciting a surah out of Qur'anic order, and omitting a surah between two surahs. The Hanafi school grades these as makruh tanzihi, based on proofs from hadith and the practice of the Companions. We will explore the reasoning and exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts under discussion
The author lists three acts: (1) reciting multiple surahs in one rak'ah, (2) reciting a surah above the order (i.e., a later surah before an earlier one), and (3) interposing a surah by omitting a small surah between two surahs in two rak'ahs.
These are specific to fard prayer; nafl prayer is exempt.
2
Determine the hukm (ruling)
The author states these acts are makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked) in fard prayer. They are not haram and do not invalidate the prayer, but should be avoided.
The ruling is based on the principle of avoiding hardship for the congregation and maintaining respect for the Qur'anic order.
3
Examine the primary proof
The hadith from Abu Dawood (no. 795) commands the imam to lighten the prayer due to the presence of sick, elderly, and those with needs. Reciting multiple surahs lengthens the prayer, contradicting this command.
The imperative 'falyukhaffif' indicates a recommendation, not obligation, hence the ruling is makruh rather than haram.
4
Analyze the companion and tabi'i sayings
Additional proofs: a companion forbade joining two surahs in one rak'ah; a tabi'i disliked reciting part of a verse and leaving part; another companion considered reversing order as a sign of a reversed heart.
These sayings reinforce the dislike but also show it was a known practice among the early Muslims.
5
Note the exceptions
The author states that if one forgets or has a valid excuse (e.g., not memorizing a long surah), the act is not makruh. Also, skipping a long surah is not disliked because not everyone can memorize it.
The exceptions prevent undue hardship and acknowledge human limitations.

فصل ما يكره للمصلى من الفرض وقراءة سورة فوق التي قرأها وفصله بسورة بين سورتين قرأهما في ركعتين

مختصر کرتے تھے۔

ترجمه : (۵۶۰) فرض کی ایک رکعت میں مکر رسورت پڑھنا، او پر کی سورت پڑھنا، دورکعت میں دوسورتوں کے مابین ایک چھوٹی سورت کا فاصلہ کرنا۔

تشریح : فرض کی رکعت میں کئی سورتیں پڑھے گا تو رکعت لمبی ہو جائے گی، جس سے مقتدی کو تکلیف ہوگی اس لئے ایک رکعت میں کئی کئی سورتیں پڑھنا مکروہ ہے۔ قرآن کریم ترتیب کے ساتھ لکھا ہوا ہے، اس کے خلاف الٹی ترتیب سے پڑھنا خلاف ترتیب ہے اس لئے مکروہ تنزیہی ہے، مثلا پہلی رکعت میں اذا جاء نصر اللہ، پڑھے اور دوسری رکعت میں قل یا ایھا الکافرون، پڑھے یہ مکروہ ہے ۔ دو چھوٹی سورتوں کے درمیان ایک چھوٹی سورت چھوڑنے سے اس کی بے اعتنائی معلوم ہوتی ہے اور ایک قسم کی تو ہین ہے ،مثلا پہلی رکعت میں انا اعطیناک الکوثر ، پڑھے اور دوسری رکعت میں اذا جاء نصر اللہ ، پڑھے اور بیچ میں قبل یا ایھا الکافرون کو چھوڑ دے تو یہ اس کی تو ہین ہے اس لئے بغیر کسی مجبوری کے چھوڑ دینا مکروہ ہے ، ہاں یاد نہ ہو یا کوئی مجبوری ہو تو مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ یا بڑی سورت چھوڑ دے تو مکروہ نہیں ہے، کیونکہ اتنی بڑی سورت ہر کسی کو یاد نہیں ہوتی۔ وجه : (۱) مکر رسورت پڑھنا مکروہ ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابی هـريـــة ان النبي الله قال اذا صلى احدكم للناس فليخفف فان فيهم السقيم و الشيخ الكبير و ذو الحاجة ـ (ابوداود شریف ، باب تخفیف الصلاة، ص۱۲۴، نمبر ۷۹۵) (۲) یہ قول صحابی بھی ہے۔ عن ابی جعفر قال لا يقرن بين سورتين في كل ركعة _(مصنف ابن ابی شبية ، باب من كان لا تجمع بين السورتین فی رکعۃ ، ج اول ص ۳۲۴ نمبر ۳۷۰۵) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ ایک رکعت میں دوسورتیں نہیں پڑھنی چاہئے۔ ہاں نفل میں جتنی چاہے سورتیں پڑھے ۔ (۳) عن عبد الله بن ابي الهذيل قال كانوا يكرهون ان يقرأوا بعض الآية ويتركوا بعضها - (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من کره ان يقر البعض الآية ويترك بعضها ، ج سادس ص ۱۵۱، نمبر ۳۰۲۵۵) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ درمیان سے بعض آیت چھوڑ نا مکروہ ہے۔ (۴) عن شقيق قال قيل لعبد الله ان فلانا يقرأ القرآن منكوسا ، فقال عبد الله ذاك منكوس القلب ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من کره ان يقرا القرآن منكوسا ، ج سادس، ص ۱۵۵، نمبر ۳۰۲۹۸) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ قرآن الٹا پڑھنا دل کے الٹے ہونے کی دلیل ہے۔
Chapter: What is disliked for the one praying [in fard prayer]: Reciting multiple surahs, reciting a surah above [the order] of what he recited, and interposing a surah between two surahs that he has recited in two rak'ahs. [Then Urdu commentary:] Translation (560): Reciting multiple surahs in one rak'ah of fard, reciting a surah above [the order], and separating two surahs with a small surah in two rak'ahs. Explanation: If one recites multiple surahs in a fard rak'ah, the rak'ah will become long, causing hardship for the followers, therefore reciting multiple surahs in one rak'ah is makruh. The Qur'an is written in sequence; reciting in reverse order contradicts the order, hence it is makruh tanzihi, e.g., reciting Surah an-Nasr in the first rak'ah and Surah al-Kafirun in the second rak'ah is makruh. Leaving a small surah between two small surahs shows disregard and is a kind of disrespect, e.g., reciting Surah al-Kawthar in the first rak'ah and Surah an-Nasr in the second, omitting Surah al-Kafirun from between, this is disrespect, so omitting without excuse is makruh; but if one forgets or has an excuse, it is not makruh. Or if one leaves a long surah, it is not makruh because not everyone remembers such a long surah. Proofs: (1) Reciting multiple surahs is makruh based on this hadith: from Abu Hurayra that the Prophet ﷺ said, 'When one of you leads people in prayer, let him lighten it, for among them are the sick, the elderly, and those with needs.' (Abu Dawood, chapter on lightening prayer, p.124, no.795) (2) This is also a saying of a companion: from Abu Ja'far: 'He said: Do not join two surahs in one rak'ah.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, chapter on those who did not combine two surahs in one rak'ah, vol.1, p.324, no.3705) (3) From 'Abdullah ibn Abi al-Hudhayl: 'He said: They used to dislike reciting part of a verse and leaving part of it.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, chapter on those who disliked reciting part of a verse and leaving part, vol.6, p.151, no.30255) (4) From Shaqiq: 'It was said to 'Abdullah: So-and-so recites the Qur'an upside down. 'Abdullah said: That is an upside-down heart.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, chapter on those who disliked reciting the Qur'an upside down, vol.6, p.155, no.30298) This companion's saying indicates that reciting the Qur'an in reverse is evidence of a reversed heart.
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proofs (ruling_with_proof) from the chapter on disliked acts in prayer. The author explains three related actions that are makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked) in fard prayer: (1) reciting multiple surahs in one rak'ah, (2) reciting a surah out of its proper order (e.g., a later surah before an earlier one), and (3) leaving a gap by omitting a surah between two surahs. The ruling applies specifically to fard prayer; in nafl prayer, one may recite as many surahs as desired. The author provides four proofs: a hadith from Abu Dawood about lightening the prayer for the congregation, a companion narration from Ibn Abi Shayba forbidding joining two surahs, a narration from a tabi'i (follower) about not reciting part of a verse, and a companion saying that reversing the order indicates a reversed heart. The author also clarifies exceptions: if one forgets or has a valid excuse, it is not makruh; also, skipping a long surah is not makruh as it is not memorized by everyone.

Key Terms
مکروہ تنزیہی (makruh tanzihi): A disliked act that is not sinful but better avoided; close to halal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Haram
B) Makruh tanzihi
C) Mubah
D) Wajib

Key Takeaway
Reciting multiple surahs, reversing order, or omitting surahs in fard prayer is makruh tanzihi, with exceptions for forgetfulness and long surahs.

Ruling on Smelling Perfume and Fanning in Prayer
Ruling on smelling perfume and fanning in prayer with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on intentionally smelling perfume and fanning during prayer, and explain the evidence from hadith and qiyas.

Core Idea
Unnecessary actions in prayer that risk excessive movement are makruh tanzih.

In this lesson, we examine two specific actions in prayer that are considered disliked (makruh): deliberately smelling perfume and fanning oneself. The text distinguishes between incidental scent and deliberate action, and provides proofs from hadith and the practice of the salaf. Understanding these rulings helps preserve the khushu' of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act? The text mentions two acts: (1) intentionally smelling perfume during prayer, and (2) fanning oneself with cloth or fan. The ruling given is that both are makruh (disliked). However, note the condition: if the scent reaches without intention, it is not makruh.
Intentional action is key.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'I was commanded to prostrate on seven bones, and not to gather my hair or garment.' This hadith prohibits unnecessary handling of clothing during prayer.
The hadith is from Sahih Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Apply qiyas
The prohibition of gathering the garment is extended to smelling perfume and fanning by analogy. The common 'illa (effective cause) is unnecessary movement that risks excessive movement (amal kathir) and compromises khushu'.
Qiyas is valid because the 'illa is present in both the original and new cases.
4
Consider the secondary dalil
The athar of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i specifically states that he disliked fanning with the garment during prayer. This supports the ruling by the practice of a prominent tabi'i.
This is a qawl sahabi (or tabi'i) used as supportive evidence.
5
Determine the thamarah
The practical consequence: the actions are makruh tanzih, not haram. They do not invalidate the prayer but are to be avoided for better concentration.
The ruling is a matter of dislike, not prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۵۶۱) خوشبو سونگھنا، کپڑے یا پنکھے سے ایک یا دو بار ہوا کرنا۔

تشریح : کپڑے یا بدن میں خوشبو لگی ہوئی ہو اور اسکی بوناک میں آ رہی ہو یہ مکروہ نہیں ہے لیکن قصدا انگلی کو ناک میں لیجا کر سونگھنا عمل کثیر کا خطرہ ہے اس لئے یہ مکروہ ہے۔ کپڑے یا پنکھے سے نماز میں ہوا کرنا عمل کثیر کا خطرہ ہے، اور یہ محسوس ہوتا ہے کہ یہ کپڑے سے کھیل رہا ہے اس لئے یہ خشوع و خضوع کے خلاف ہے اس لئے مکروہ ہے۔ وجه :(1) عن ابن عباس عن النبي الله قال امرت ان اسجد على سبعة اعظم لا اكف شعرا ولا ثوبا ( بخاری شریف ، باب لا يكف ثوبه فی الصلوۃ ، ص ۱۱۳، نمبر ۸۱۶ مسلم شریف، باب اعضاء السجو دو انھی عن كف الشعر والثوب، ص ۱۹۳، نمبر ۴۹۰ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ کپڑے کو بلاوجہ بار بار سمیٹنا مکروہ ہے تو خوشبو سونگھنا بھی مکروہ ہوگا۔ (۲) ابراهيم انه كان يكره ان يتروح في الصلاة يعني بثوبه من الحر (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب الترويح في الصلاة ، ج ثانی ص ۱۷۹، نمبر ۳۳۵۶) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ کپڑے سے ہوا کرنا مکروہ ہے۔
Translation (561): Smelling perfume, and fanning with cloth or fan once or twice. Explanation: If perfume is applied to the cloth or body and its scent reaches [the nose] without intention, it is not makruh. But deliberately bringing the finger to the nose to smell involves the risk of excessive movement, therefore it is makruh. Fanning in prayer with cloth or fan incurs the risk of excessive movement, and it appears as if one is playing with the cloth, so it is against khushu' and khudhu', therefore it is makruh. Proofs: (1) From Ibn 'Abbas from the Prophet ﷺ: 'I was commanded to prostrate on seven bones, and not to gather my hair or garment.' (Bukhari, chapter on not gathering the garment in prayer, p.113, no.816; Muslim, chapter on limbs of prostration and prohibition of gathering hair and garment, p.193, no.490) This hadith indicates that repeatedly gathering the garment unnecessarily is makruh, so smelling perfume is also makruh by analogy. (2) Ibrahim [al-Nakha'i] disliked fanning in prayer, i.e., with his garment from heat. (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on fanning in prayer, vol.2, p.179, no.3356) This saying of a tabi'i indicates that fanning with the garment is makruh.
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs (ruling_with_proof) about two disliked actions: deliberately smelling perfume and fanning oneself during prayer. The author distinguishes between perfume that reaches the nose without action (not makruh) and deliberately bringing the hand to the nose (makruh due to risk of excessive movement). Fanning is also makruh because it involves potentially excessive movement and appears playful, undermining khushu'. Two proofs are provided: a hadith forbidding gathering the garment unnecessarily, and a narration of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i disliking fanning. The text notes that once or twice is mentioned, implying lesser frequency is less problematic, but still disliked.

Key Terms
عمل کثیر (amal kathir): Excessive action that disrupts the form of prayer, often leading to nullification.
خشوع (khushu'): Humility and concentration in prayer.

Disliked Acts in Prayer: Turning Digits and Hand Placement
Ruling with proofs on two disliked actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on turning digits away from qibla and omitting hand placement on knees in prayer, identify the supporting hadith proofs, and apply the Hanafi hierarchy of sunnah to determine that such omissions are makruh tanzihi.

Core Idea
Contradicting the Prophet's sunnah in prayer posture is makruh tanzihi, not invalidating but disliked.

Prayer has many sunnah actions that complete its form and reward. Among them are pointing your fingers and toes toward the qibla during prostration, and placing your hands on your knees with a firm grasp during bowing. The Hanafi school classifies these as sunnah — actions the Prophet consistently performed. Deliberately omitting them without excuse is makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked). In this lesson, we examine the textual proofs for these two rulings and learn how to apply the sunnah-makruh hierarchy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts and their rulings
From the passage, note two specific acts: (1) turning the fingers of hands and feet away from the qibla during sujud (and other positions), and (2) not placing the hands on the knees during ruku. Both are described as makruh because they contradict the sunnah.
The passage states these are 'sunnah' acts, so doing the opposite is 'makruh'.
2
Locate the three hadith proofs
The author cites three proofs: a hadith from Bukhari about facing the feet to qibla, a narration from 'Aisha in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba about hand placement in sujud, and a hadith from Tirmidhi describing the Prophet's hand position in ruku as if grasping the knees.
These ahadith establish the Prophet's consistent practice (fi'l), which in Hanafi usul indicates sunnah.
3
Trace how each proof establishes sunnah
The Prophet's action (fi'l) is a source of sunnah. When he consistently performed an act, doing it becomes sunnah, and deliberately omitting it without reason becomes makruh tanzihi. For example, the Bukhari hadith shows he faced his feet to qibla, so contradicting that is contrary to an established practice.
Hanafi usul: al-fi'l al-mustamirr yufidu al-sunnah.
4
Distinguish between fard, wajib, sunnah, and makruh
In Hanafi fiqh, omitting a sunnah does not invalidate prayer nor require sajdah sahw; it only attracts dislike (karahah tanzihiyyah) if done habitually. This is different from leaving a wajib (needs compensation) or a fard (invalidates).
The hukm level here is makruh tanzihi, confirmed by the mufta bihi position.
5
Apply the ruling in daily prayer
Ensure during sujud you point your fingers and toes toward the qibla, and during ruku grasp your knees with hands as if holding them. If you occasionally forget, no sin, but deliberately abandoning these sunnah acts is disliked.
The modern application: even in tight spaces, try to align digits toward qibla as much as possible.

Source Text

ترجمه : (۵۶۲) سجدے وغیرہ میں ہاتھ پاؤں کی انگلیاں قبلہ سے پھرانا، اور رکوع میں دونوں ہاتھوں کا گھٹنوں پر رکھنا چھوڑ دینا۔

تشریح : سجدے میں ہاتھ پاؤں کی انگلیاں قبلہ کی طرف کرنا سنت ہے اس لئے اس کے خلاف کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ رکوع میں دونوں ہاتھوں کو گھٹنے پر اس طرح رکھے کہ گویا کہ اس کو پکڑے ہوا ہو، یہ سنت ہے اس لئے ہاتھوں کو گھٹنوں پر نہ رکھے یہ مکروہ ہوگا۔

عن عائشة قالت كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا سجد وضع يديه وجاه القبلة . (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من كان يقول اذا سجد فلیوجہ ید یہ الی القبلة ، ج ثانی ص ۲۳۶ نمبر ۱۲ ۲۷) اس لئے اس کے خلاف مکروہ ہوگا۔(۳) اور گھٹنے پر ہاتھ نہ رکھے یہ مکروہ ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ فذكروا صلوۃ رسول الله الله الله فقال ابو حميد انا اعلمكم بصلوة رسول الله الله ان رسول الله علم ركع فوضع يديه على ركبتيه كانه قابض عليهما و وتر يديه فنحاهما عن جنبيه. ( ترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء بیجافی یدیہ عن جنبیہ فی الرکوع ، ص ۷۲، نمبر ۲۶۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہاتھوں سے گھٹنوں کو اس طرح پکڑے کہ کمان کی رسی کی طرح معلوم ہو
Translation (562): Turning the fingers of the hands and feet from the qibla in prostration and otherwise, and leaving the placing of the hands on the knees in bowing. Explanation: It is sunnah to point the fingers of the hands and feet towards the qibla in prostration, so doing contrary is makruh. In ruku', one should place both hands on the knees as if grasping them; this is sunnah, so not placing the hands on the knees is makruh. Proofs: (1) It is makruh to place fingers opposite to the qibla, based on the hadith: 'Abu Hamid said from the Prophet ﷺ: He would face the tips of his feet towards the qibla.' (Bukhari, chapter on facing the tips of the feet to the qibla, p.131, no.808) (2) From 'Aisha: 'When the Prophet ﷺ prostrated, he would place his hands facing the qibla.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, chapter on facing the hands to the qibla in prostration, vol.2, p.236, no.12227) So contrary is makruh. (3) Not placing the hands on the knees is makruh, based on the hadith: 'They mentioned the prayer of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, so Abu Hamid said: I am most knowledgeable of the prayer of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ. The Messenger of Allah ﷺ bowed and placed his hands on his knees as if grasping them, and he separated his hands from his sides.' (Tirmidhi, chapter on keeping the hands away from the sides in ruku', p.72, no.260) This indicates that one should grasp the knees such that they appear like the string of a bow.
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs (ruling_with_proof) about two disliked acts: (1) turning the fingers of hands and feet away from the qibla during prostration and other positions, and (2) not placing the hands on the knees during ruku'. The author explains that pointing digits towards the qibla is sunnah, so deviation is makruh. Similarly, gripping the knees in ruku' is sunnah, so omission is makruh. Three proofs are given: a hadith from Bukhari about facing the feet towards qibla, a narration from 'Aisha about hand placement in sujud, and a hadith from Tirmidhi describing the Prophet's hand position in ruku'. The text emphasizes that these are established sunnah practices.

Key Terms
سنت (sunnah): A recommended action that the Prophet consistently performed; leaving it without reason is makruh tanzihi.
مکروہ (makruh): An act that is disliked but not sinful; avoiding it brings reward; doing it is not punished.

Key Takeaway

Disliked Acts in Prayer: Yawning, Closing Eyes, Looking Up, Stretching
Ruling on four disliked acts in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on four disliked acts in prayer and explain why they are makruh tanzih based on the hadith.

Core Idea
Acts that oppose khushu' in prayer are makruh tanzih.

In this lesson, we examine four actions that the Hanafi school considers makruh during prayer: yawning, closing the eyes, looking up to the sky, and stretching. These acts are disliked because they conflict with the required state of humility (khushu' and khudhu'). Understanding why they are disliked helps maintain the proper spirit of salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four acts
List the four actions mentioned as makruh: yawning, closing eyes, looking up, stretching.
2
Understand the reasoning
The text states they are signs of laziness and against khushu'. This is the basis for the ruling.
Khushu' is the essential spirit of prayer.
3
Connect the hadith proof
The hadith about yawning (from Satan, command to suppress) is used as evidence for the general ruling.
The hadith is from Muslim.
4
Determine the hukm level
The ruling is makruh tanzih (slightly disliked), not haram or invalidating.
Prayer remains valid but deficient in completeness.

Disliked Actions: Physical Positioning in Prayer
Section 562 of the chapter on makruhat al-salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on turning fingers or feet away from the qibla in sujud and on placing hands on knees in ruku, and identify the proofs from sunnah.

Core Idea
The sunnah is to face qibla with toes and place hands on knees; opposing this without necessity is makruh tanzihi.

In this section of the chapter on Makruhat al-Salah, the author lists two specific physical actions that are disliked: turning the fingers or toes away from the qibla during prostration, and not placing the hands on the knees during bowing. These actions contradict the established sunnah of the Prophet ﷺ. The author provides hadith evidence from Bukhari, Ibn Abi Shaybah, and Tirmidhi to show the prophetic practice. Understanding these rulings helps a Muslim perfect his prayer by avoiding even minor deviations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actions
List the two actions mentioned: (1) turning fingers or toes away from qibla in sujud and elsewhere, (2) not placing hands on knees in ruku.
2
State the ruling
The ruling for both is makruh tanzihi (disliked, not prohibitive) because they contradict the sunnah but do not invalidate prayer.
3
Examine the proof
The author cites a hadith from Abu Humayd that the Prophet placed his hands on his knees in ruku, and from Aisha that he placed his hands towards qibla in sujud. Not following this is makruh.
Note the chain: these are sahih hadith.
4
Understand the thamarah
The practical consequence is that doing these actions is not sinful but is disliked; the prayer remains valid but lacking perfection.

فصل ما يكره للمصلى (۵۶۲) وتحویل اصابع يديه او رجليه عن القبلة في السجود وغيره وترک وضع الیدین علی الركبتين في الركوع (۵۶۳) والتثاؤب و تغميض عينيه ورفعهما للسماء والتمطى (۵۶۴) والعمل القليل واخذ قملة وقتلها وتغطية انفه وفمه ووضع شيء في فمه يمنع القراءة. ترجمه: (۵۶۲) سجدے وغیرہ میں ہاتھ پاؤں کی انگلیاں قبلہ سے پھرانا، اور رکوع میں دونوں ہاتھوں کا گھٹنوں پر رکھنا چھوڑ دینا۔ تشریح: سجدے میں ہاتھ پاؤں کی انگلیاں قبلہ کی طرف کرنا سنت ہے اس لئے اس کے خلاف کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ رکوع میں دونوں ہاتھوں کو گھٹنے پر اس طرح رکھے کہ گویا کہ اس کو پکڑے ہوا ہو، یہ سنت ہے اس لئے ہاتھوں کو گھٹنوں پر نہ رکھے یہ مکروہ ہوگا۔ وجه: (۱) قبلہ کے خلاف انگلیاں رکھنا مکروہ ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ يستقبـل بـاطـراف رجليه القبلة قال ابو حميد عن النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم. (بخاری شریف، باب يستقبل باطراف رجلیہ القبلۃ، ص ۱۳۱ نمبر ۸۰۸) (۲) عن عائشة قالت كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا سجد وضع يديه وجاه القبلة. (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ، باب من كان يقول اذا سجد فلیوجہ یدیہ الی القبلة، ج ثانی ص ۲۳۶ نمبر ۱۲۲۷) (۳) اور گھٹنے پر ہاتھ نہ رکھے یہ مکروہ ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ فذكروا صلوۃ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال ابو حميد انا اعلمكم بصلوة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ركع فوضع يديه على ركبتيه كانه قابض عليهما و وتر يديه فنحاهما عن جنبيه. (ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی تجافی یدیہ عن جنبیہ فی الرکوع، ص ۷۲، نمبر ۲۶۰) ترجمه: (۵۶۳) جمائی لینا، آنکھیں بند رکھنا، آنکھیں آسمان کی طرف اٹھانا، انگڑائی لینا۔ تشریح: یہ سب باتیں سستی کی علامت ہیں اور خشوع و خضوع کے خلاف ہیں اس لئے یہ سب مکروہ ہیں۔ وجه: (۱) عن ابي هريرة ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال التثاوب من الشيطان فاذا تثاوب أحدكم فليكظم ما استطاع. (مسلم شریف، باب تشميت العاطس و کراھیة التثاوب، ص۱۲۹۴، نمبر ۲۹۹۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جمائی کو حتی الوسع دور کرے، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ بلا وجہ یہ کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ (۲) آنکھیں بند نہ کرے اس کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے۔ روینا عن مجاهد وقتادة كانا يكرهان تغميض العينين في الصلاة. (سنن بیہقی، باب لا یجاوز بصره موضع سجوده، ج ثانی ص ۴۰۳ نمبر ۳۵۴۵ / مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ، باب فی تغمیض العین فی الصلاۃ، ج ثانی ص ۶۴ نمبر ۶۵۰۳) (۳) آنکھیں آسمان کی طرف نہ اٹھائے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ ان انس بن مالک حدثه قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ما بال اقوام يرفعون أبصارهم الى السماء في صلاتهم؟ فاشتد قوله فی ذالک حتی قال لينتهين عن ذالك او لتخطفن ابصارهم. (بخاری شریف، باب رفع البصر الى السماء فی الصلاۃ ص ۱۳۲، نمبر ۷۵۰ / مسلم شریف، باب النھی عن رفع البصر الى السماء فی الصلاۃ ص ۱۸۳ نمبر ۹۶۶/۴۲۸) (۴) انگڑائی نہ لے اس کے لئے یہ اثر ہے۔ قلت لعطاء الرجل يتمطى في الصلاة؟ قال لم يبلغنى فيه شيء و لكنى لا احبه، قلت فيقعقع الرقبة والاصابع و غير ذالک فی الصلاة؟ قال اكرهه، قلت التنخع او الامتخاط و البزاق وادخال الرجل يده فى انفه؟ قال لا تفعله في الصلاة، قلت فالاحتكاك في الصلاة و الارتداد و الاتزار في الصلاة؟ قال كل ذالك لا تفعله في الصلاة. (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب التحریک فی الصلاۃ، ج ثانی ص ۱۷۱، نمبر ۳۳۰۴) لغت: رکبتہ: گھٹنا۔ التثاؤب: جمائی لینا۔ تغمیض: آنکھ بند کرنا۔ التمطی: انگڑائی لینا۔ ترجمه: (۵۶۴) عمل قلیل کرنا، جوں پکڑنا اور اس کا مارنا، ناک اور منھ ڈھکنا، منھ میں ایسی چیز رکھنا جو قرأت مسنونہ کو مانع ہو۔ تشریح: عمل کثیر سے نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی، البتہ بغیر مجبوری کے عمل قلیل کرنا مکروہ ہے، جس کام کے کرنے میں ایک ہاتھ استعمال ہوتا ہو وہ عمل قلیل ہے۔ باقی سب آسان ہیں۔ وجه: (۱) جوں پکڑنے میں عمل قلیل ہوگا جو مکروہ ہے۔ جوں کا پکڑنا اور اس کو مارنا مکروہ ہے اس کیلئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن رجل من الانصار ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال اذا وجد احدكم القملة و هو يصلى فلا يقتلها و لكن يصرها حتى يصلى. (سنن بیہقی، باب من وجد فی صلاتہ قمله فصرها الخ، ج ثانی، ص ۱۴۱۸، نمبر ۳۶۰۷) (۲) ناک ڈھانپنا مکروہ ہے اس لئے یہ قول صحابی ہے۔ ان ابن عباس كره تغطية الانف، قال قتادة و كان سعيد بن المسيب و النخعی و عطاء يكرهونه. (مصنف ابن ابى شيبة، باب في تغطیة الانف وحده، ج ثانی، ص۱۳۲، نمبر ۷۳۱۲) (۳) منہ ڈھانپنا مکروہ ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے عن ابی هريرة ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نهى عن السدل في الصلوة وان يغطى الرجل فاه. (ابو داؤد شریف، باب ما جاء فی السدل فی الصلوۃ، ص ۱۰۳ نمبر ۶۴۳ / ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی کراہیۃ السدل فی الصلوۃ ص ۸۷ نمبر)
Chapter: What is disliked for the praying person. (562) Turning the fingers of his hands or his feet away from the qibla in prostration and otherwise, and leaving placing the hands on the knees in bowing. (563) Yawning, closing his eyes, raising them to the sky, and stretching. (564) Little action, catching a louse and killing it, covering his nose and mouth, and placing something in his mouth that prevents recitation. [Then Urdu translations and explanations follow, along with proofs from hadith and athar.]
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah presents the chapter on actions disliked (makruh) during prayer. The rulings are supported by hadith and statements of the Companions and Successors. The first set (562) covers physical positioning: turning the fingers or toes away from the qibla during sujud and not placing hands on knees in ruku. The second (563) lists actions indicating laziness or lack of khushu': yawning, closing eyes, looking skyward, and stretching. The third (564) addresses minimal actions like killing a louse, covering the nose or mouth, or obstructing recitation. Each is explained with proofs, emphasizing that these actions contradict the sunnah and the spirit of prayer.

Key Terms
تحویل اصابع (tahwil asabi): Turning the fingers or toes away from the qibla direction in prayer.
الركوع (al-ruku): Bowing in prayer, placing hands on knees.
القبلة (al-qibla): The direction of prayer towards the Kaaba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the proofs cited in this lesson, which action is considered makruh?
A) Placing hands on knees in ruku
B) Turning toes away from qibla in sujud
C) Looking at the place of prostration
D) Reciting Quran silently

Key Takeaway
Turning fingers or toes away from qibla and not placing hands on knees in ruku are makruh tanzihi actions that contradict sunnah but do not invalidate prayer.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
8 min
Disliked Actions: Yawning, Closing Eyes, Looking Up, and Stretching
Section 563 of the chapter on makruhat al-salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four disliked actions listed in section 563, explain the Hanafi ruling for each, and cite the hadith evidence for yawning.

Core Idea
Yawning, closing eyes, looking skyward, and stretching are makruh because they indicate laziness and contradict khushu.

Section 563 of the chapter covers four actions that stem from carelessness and distraction: yawning, closing the eyes, raising the eyes to the sky, and stretching the body. The author provides hadith and athar evidence to show that these actions are disliked. Yawning is associated with Shaytan, closing eyes is criticized by the Successors, looking up is strongly warned against by the Prophet ﷺ, and stretching is disliked based on the practice of the early Muslims. These rulings help preserve the spirit of humility in prayer.

Guided Path
1
List the four actions
Yawning (tatha'ub), closing eyes (taghmid al-'aynayn), raising eyes to sky (raf' al-basar), and stretching (tamattu).
2
State the common ruling
All are makruh tanzihi because they contravene khushu and the sunnah of focusing on the prayer.
3
Analyze the proof for yawning
The hadith in Muslim: 'Yawning is from Shaytan; when one yawns let him suppress it as much as possible.' The command to suppress indicates dislike.
The dalil is zanni in thubut but widely accepted.
4
Consider the other proofs
For closing eyes, the Successors disliked it. For looking up, the Prophet warned of loss of eyesight. For stretching, early scholars disliked it.
These proofs are weaker but sufficient for karahah tanzihiyyah.

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah presents the chapter on actions disliked (makruh) during prayer. The rulings are supported by hadith and statements of the Companions and Successors. The first set (562) covers physical positioning: turning the fingers or toes away from the qibla during sujud and not placing hands on knees in ruku. The second (563) lists actions indicating laziness or lack of khushu': yawning, closing eyes, looking skyward, and stretching. The third (564) addresses minimal actions like killing a louse, covering the nose or mouth, or obstructing recitation. Each is explained with proofs, emphasizing that these actions contradict the sunnah and the spirit of prayer.

Key Terms
التثاؤب (al-tatha'ub): Yawning; considered a disliked action in prayer because it indicates laziness and comes from Shaytan.
تغميض العينين (taghmid al-'aynayn): Closing the eyes during prayer; disliked because it prevents focusing on the prayer and resembles the practice of magicians.
التمطی (al-tamatti): Stretching the body during prayer; disliked as it indicates laziness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which hadith is used as evidence for the dislike of yawning in prayer?
A) 'Yawning is from Shaytan, so suppress it as much as possible.'
B) 'Do not raise your eyes to the sky lest they be snatched away.'
C) 'Closing the eyes in prayer is the habit of the Jews.'
D) 'Stretching in prayer is from the act of the donkey.'

Key Takeaway
Yawning, closing eyes, looking skyward, and stretching are makruh because they contradict the required humility and focus in prayer.

Disliked Actions: Minimal Actions and Covering the Face
Section 564 of the chapter on makruhat al-salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'amal qalil (minimal action), state the Hanafi ruling on killing a louse, covering the nose/mouth, and placing something in the mouth during prayer, and explain the proofs.

Core Idea
Minimal actions like killing a louse are makruh; covering the nose or mouth is also disliked because it prevents proper recitation.

Section 564 addresses actions that involve minimal movement or obstruction of the face. The key concept is that 'amal qalil (action using one hand) is generally disliked if done without necessity. The author gives specific examples: catching and killing a louse, covering the nose or mouth, and putting something in the mouth that hinders recitation. Proofs include a hadith about not killing a louse during prayer and statements of the Companions and Successors. This lesson clarifies the boundary between disliked and permissible minimal actions.

Guided Path
1
Define 'amal qalil
Minimal action is what involves one hand or a single movement; it does not destroy the form of prayer.
If it becomes excessive ('amal kathir), it invalidates prayer.
2
List the specific examples
(1) catching and killing a louse, (2) covering the nose, (3) covering the mouth, (4) placing something in the mouth that prevents recitation.
3
State the ruling for each
All are makruh tanzihi because they are unnecessary and either involve killing a living being or prevent perfect recitation.
4
Examine the proof for killing louse
The hadith: 'If any of you finds a louse while praying, let him not kill it, but rather pinch it until he finishes the prayer.' This indicates dislike of killing.
The hadith is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi.
5
Understand the proofs for covering face
Ibn Abbas disliked covering the nose, and there is a hadith forbidding covering the mouth (sedl). Also, placing something that impedes recitation is disliked because recitation is wajib.

Chapter: What is disliked for the praying person. (562) Turning the fingers of his hands or his feet away from the qibla in prostration and otherwise, and leaving placing the hands on the knees in bowing. (563) Yawning, closing his eyes, raising them to the sky, and stretching. (564) Little action, catching a louse and killing it, covering his nose and mouth, and placing something in his mouth that prevents recitation. Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah presents the chapter on actions disliked (makruh) during prayer. The rulings are supported by hadith and statements of the Companions and Successors. The first set (562) covers physical positioning: turning the fingers or toes away from the qibla during sujud and not placing hands on knees in ruku. The second (563) lists actions indicating laziness or lack of khushu': yawning, closing eyes, looking skyward, and stretching. The third (564) addresses minimal actions like killing a louse, covering the nose or mouth, or obstructing recitation. Each is explained with proofs, emphasizing that these actions contradict the sunnah and the spirit of prayer.

Key Terms
العمل القليل (al-'amal al-qalil): A minimal action, defined as using one hand; disliked if done without necessity, while excessive action (using both hands or multiple movements) invalidates prayer.
القملة (al-qamla): A louse; catching and killing it during prayer is considered makruh according to the hadith.
السدل (al-sadl): Covering the mouth or nose during prayer; forbidden or disliked due to hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Minimal actions like killing a louse and covering the nose/mouth are makruh; using one hand defines 'amal qalil, while using both hands may invalidate prayer.

Disliked Minor Actions in Prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on minor actions (amal qalil) in prayer, distinguish them from major actions (amal kathir), and identify the proofs for specific disliked actions.

Core Idea
Minor actions in prayer are makruh, not invalidating, but should be avoided.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah addresses the category of minor actions during salah that are considered makruh (disliked). It clarifies the boundary between actions that break the prayer and those that are merely discouraged. The author provides examples and supports each with authentic proofs from hadith and the practice of the Salaf. Understanding this distinction is essential for maintaining the sanctity of prayer without falling into unnecessary rigidity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall ruling
The passage states that minor actions (amal qalil) are makruh. Recognize that this is a ruling of disapproval, not invalidation.
The term makruh in Hanafi fiqh typically means makruh tanzih (disliked but not sinful) unless specified otherwise.
2
Distinguish between amal qalil and amal kathir
Note that amal kathir invalidates the prayer, while amal qalil does not. The key criterion is whether the action uses one hand or less, or if it is a movement that a bystander would not consider part of prayer.
Amal kathir is defined as using both hands or moving three consecutive times.
3
List the specific examples
The text gives five examples: taking and killing a louse, covering the nose, covering the mouth, placing something in the mouth that prevents recitation, and yawning (implied).
Each example is independently supported by a proof.
4
Examine the proof for each example
For lice, a hadith instructs to pinch rather than kill. For covering nose, the practice of Ibn Abbas and others. For covering mouth, a hadith of prohibition. For yawning, a hadith advising to suppress it.
The proofs vary in strength but all lead to the ruling of karahah.
5
Determine the level of karahah
Based on the wording, these are makruh tanzih. Some actions might be makruh tahrimi if the prohibition is explicit, but the text does not indicate that.
The Hanafi principle is that nahy (prohibition) indicates tanzih unless there is evidence for tahrim.
