Section: What is disliked for the one praying. (564) Minor actions, taking a louse and killing it, covering his nose and mouth, and placing something in his mouth that prevents recitation. ... [followed by Urdu explanations and Arabic proofs]
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof section on disliked (makruh) actions in prayer. The text states that minor actions (amal qalil) are makruh, while many actions (amal kathir) invalidate the prayer. Minor actions are defined as those performed with one hand. Specific examples include taking and killing a louse, covering the nose and mouth, and placing something in the mouth that prevents proper recitation. The commentary provides proofs for each: for lice, a hadith instructing not to kill it but to pinch it; for covering the nose, the practice of Ibn Abbas and others; for covering the mouth, a hadith prohibiting it; and for placing something in the mouth, a narration from the Prophet prohibiting covering the mouth. The overall ruling is that these actions are makruh tanzih (disliked but not sinful) without necessity.

Key Terms
عمل قلیل (amal qalil): A minor action in prayer, typically using one hand or less, that does not break the prayer but is disliked.
عمل کثیر (amal kathir): A significant action that breaks the prayer, such as using both hands or moving three times consecutively.
تثاؤب (tattha'ub): Yawning. It is disliked during prayer and should be suppressed if possible.
تغميض (taghmid): Closing the eyes. It is disliked during prayer based on the practice of some Tabi'un.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on taking a louse during prayer?
A) It invalidates the prayer because it is a major action.
B) It is permissible and recommended.
C) It is disliked (makruh) and one should pinch it rather than kill it.
D) It is prohibited (haram) because it harms a living creature.

Key Takeaway
Minor actions (amal qalil) in prayer are makruh tanzih; they do not invalidate the prayer but should be avoided, especially when unnecessary.

Disliked Acts in Prostration: Turban, Image, Forehead Only
States the ruling on prostration on turban fold, on an image, and on forehead alone without excuse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three disliked acts in prostration according to the Hanafi school, identify the proof (dalil) for each, and apply the ruling to new scenarios.

Core Idea
Prostration on turban fold or an image, or omitting the nose without excuse, is makruh tanzih.

In this lesson, we examine three specific disliked actions during prostration: prostrating on the folded part of the turban, on a surface bearing a picture of a living being, and prostrating only on the forehead while leaving the nose off the ground without a valid excuse. The Hanafi school rules these as makruh tanzih (slightly disliked) – the prayer remains valid but is deficient. We will explore the textual proofs and the reasoning behind each ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three disliked acts
The text lists three: (1) sujud on the kawr (folded part) of the turban, (2) sujud on an image (surah), and (3) restricting prostration to the forehead alone while omitting the nose without an excuse.
The third act implies that both forehead and nose are required, but the nose is secondary.
2
Determine the ruling level for each
All three are ruled makruh tanzih (slightly disliked). The prayer is valid but incomplete. The text explains why: for the turban, it involves extra movement; for the image, it is prohibited; for omitting the nose, it contradicts the sunnah.
In extreme heat or cold, sujud on the turban is permissible, but disliked if it requires unnecessary movement.
3
Examine the proof (dalil) for each
For the turban: a qawl sahabi from Ibn Umar disliked it. For the image: the hadith of Aisha about the Prophet's severe warning against image-makers. For the nose: the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet was commanded to prostrate on seven bones, including the forehead and nose, and another hadith that there is no prayer if the nose does not touch the ground.
The hadith about seven bones is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for wujub in the Hanafi school.
4
Understand the wajh al-dalalah (evidential link)
The command to prostrate on the nose (via the Prophet's gesture) and the explicit statement that prayer is incomplete without placing the nose indicate that omission without excuse makes the prostration deficient, hence disliked. The prohibition of images makes prostrating on them indirectly associated with the haram, so it is disliked.
The nose is not a rukn (pillar) but a wajib (obligatory element); omitting it does not invalidate but requires compensation (sajdah sahw) if done intentionally? Actually here it is disliked, not requiring sajdah sahw.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference and mufta bihi
The Hanafi position is that these acts are makruh tanzih. Other schools might consider prostrating on turban fold permissible without dislike, or consider omitting the nose as invalidating. The mufta bihi (operative opinion) is the Hanafi ruling: makruh tanzih, prayer valid.
The text does not engage in a detailed dispute but the cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.

(565) And prostration on the folded part of his turban, and on an image, and restricting to the forehead without excuse from the nose... [followed by Urdu explanations and Arabic proofs]
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof section on three disliked actions in prostration: (1) prostrating on the folded part of the turban (kawr al-‘imamah), (2) prostrating on an image (surah), and (3) limiting prostration to the forehead alone while omitting the nose without an excuse. The commentary explains that prostrating on the turban fold is disliked because it involves minor action; in extreme heat or cold it may be permissible but otherwise it is makruh. Prostrating on an image is makruh because images are haram in general. Restricting to the forehead is makruh because both forehead and nose are required for proper sujud; the nose is a secondary part. The proofs include the practice of Ibn ‘Umar (disliking sujud on turban fold), the hadith of ‘A’ishah about pictures, and the hadith of Ibn ‘Abbas stating the Prophet was commanded to prostrate on seven bones, including the forehead and nose, and another hadith that there is no prayer for one who does not place his nose on the ground.

Key Terms
كور العمامة (kawr al-'imamah): The folded part of the turban on which one might prostrate instead of the bare forehead.
المسجد على صورة (al-sujud 'ala surah): Prostrating on a surface that has a picture of a living being.
الجبهة (al-jabhah): The forehead, the primary part for prostration.
الانف (al-anf): The nose, required to touch the ground during prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It invalidates the prayer.
B) It is permissible and recommended.
C) It is makruh tanzih (slightly disliked).
D) It is haram and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
Prostration on a turban fold, on an image, or on the forehead alone without the nose is makruh tanzih – the prayer remains valid but is deficient.

The Seven Disliked Places for Prayer
Hadith listing seven disliked places for prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven places where prayer is makruh, explain the Hanafi ruling of makruh tanzihi, and apply the ruling to identify similar places.

Core Idea
Prayer in these seven places is disliked but valid; the prohibition is karahah, not tahrim.

This lesson introduces a hadith listing seven specific places where the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade prayer. The Hanafi school interprets this prohibition as makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked), meaning the prayer is valid but it is better to avoid these locations. We will examine the hadith, the reasoning behind the ruling, and how to apply it in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the seven places
Read the hadith and list the seven places mentioned: rubbish dump, slaughterhouse, graveyard, middle of the road, bathhouse, camel resting places, and on top of the Kaaba.
The term 'bathhouse' refers to public baths with impurity.
2
Classify the ruling level
The hadith uses a prohibition (نهى). In Hanafi usul, a prohibition from an ahad hadith indicates karahah tanzihiyyah, not haram. Determine why the Hanafi rule says makruh, not haram or invalid.
The hadith is ahad (single-transmission), so its evidence is zanni; thus, the ruling is below the level of wujub.
3
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
Each place has a specific reason for dislike: impurity, disturbance, danger of shirk (graveyard), or disrespect (on top of Kaaba). Reflect on why the school considers the prayer valid despite these factors.
The dislike is not due to the place itself but the context.
4
Apply to new cases
Think of modern equivalents: rubbish dump = landfill, slaughterhouse = abattoir, bathhouse = public showers, etc. Does the ruling extend to similar places?
Use qiyas: if the  illa (reason) is present, the ruling applies.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars consider it makruh tahrimi or even invalid (e.g., on top of Kaaba). Understand that the Hanafi position is that prayer remains valid but disliked.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both views have proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وجه : (۱) عن ابن عمر ان النبى الله الله نهى ان يصلى في سبعة مواطن : فى المزبلة و المجزرة و المقبرة و قارعة الطريق، و في الحمام و فى مواطن الابل و فوق ظهر بیت الله - ترندی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی کرابیته ما یصلی الیہ وفیہ ص ۹۴ نمبر ۳۴۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ راستے کے درمیان ، حمام خانہ ، قبرستان ، اور بیت الخلاء میں نماز نہ پڑھو۔ لغت : الحمام: پچھلے زمانے میں غسل خانہ بنا ہوتا تھا جس میں سب نہاتے تھے، اس میں عمو ما بد بو ہوتی تھی ۔ المخرج: نکلنے کی جگہ، مراد ہے پیخانہ کرنے کی جگہ۔
Chapter: What is disliked for the one praying. Proof: (1) From Ibn Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade praying in seven places: in the rubbish dump, the slaughterhouse, the graveyard, the middle of the road, the bathhouse, the resting places of camels, and on top of the House of Allah. (Tirmidhi Sharif, chapter on what is disliked in prayer, p. 94 no. 346) This hadith states: do not pray in the middle of the road, bathhouse, graveyard, or restroom. Lexicon: al-hammam: a bathhouse built in former times where people bathed, usually having bad odor. al-makhraj: place of exit, meaning the place of defecation.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on disliked matters for the person praying. The author first presents a hadith listing seven specific places where the Prophet forbade prayer. The Hanafi ruling is that prayer in these places is makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked) because the hadith's prohibition is taken as discouragement rather than absolute invalidity. The commentary explains the reasoning: the middle of the road causes inconvenience, the bathhouse and graveyard involve impurity or risk of shirk. The prayer itself remains valid if performed, but it is better to avoid these places.

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): A disliked act that is not sinful but better to avoid; here applied to places for prayer.
قارعة الطريق (qari'atu al-tariq): The middle of the road where people walk, causing disturbance.
حمام (hammam): A public bathhouse often containing impurities and nakedness.

Salah — Prayer

Prayer While Needing to Relieve Oneself or with Minor Impurity
Rulings on praying while in need of relieving oneself or with minor impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying while needing to relieve oneself or with minor impurity, identify the proof texts, and apply the dirham exemption rule.

Core Idea
Prayer while suppressing natural needs or with minor impurity is valid but disliked unless time or congregation is lost.

This lesson addresses two common situations: praying while needing to relieve oneself (urine, stool, or wind) and praying while carrying a small amount of impurity. The Hanafi school classifies both as makruh tanzihi—valid but disliked—unless one fears missing the prayer time or congregation. We will examine the textual proofs and the precise measurement of the excused impurity, known as the dirham exemption.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The passage addresses two distinct rulings: (a) prayer while repelling one of the two evils (urine or stool) or wind, and (b) prayer with non-preventing impurity (najasah ghayr mani'ah) – impurity that is less than the excused amount.
Both share the same basic ruling but have different proofs.
2
Understand the default ruling
The default Hanafi ruling for both cases is makruh tanzihi (disliked but not prohibited). The prayer is valid, but it is better to remove the need or impurity before praying.
The exception: if one fears losing the time or congregation, the dislike drops and it becomes permissible.
3
Analyze the proofs
The proofs cited: (1) Hadith of Aisha: 'لا صلاة بحضرة الطعام ولا هو يدافعه الاخبثان' – interpreted as negation of perfection, not invalidity. (2) Hadith of Ibn Umar: 'اذا كان احدكم على الطعام فلا يعجل حتى يقضي حاجته' – shows priority of relieving oneself. (3) Hadith of Abu Hurairah: 'تعاد الصلوة من قدر الدرهم من الدم' – sets the dirham limit for thick impurity.
The phrase 'لا صلاة' is understood as 'no complete prayer', hence valid but disliked.
4
Apply the dirham exemption
The dirham exemption distinguishes between thin (liquid) and thick (solid) impurity. For thin impurity, the area is considered (approx. 2.75 cm in diameter). For thick impurity, the weight is considered (approx. 4.374 grams). If the impurity is less than these amounts, it is excused.
If the impurity exceeds the dirham limit, the prayer becomes invalid (batil) unless removed.
5
Note the exception for necessity
If delaying relieves oneself would cause missing the congregation or the prayer time, one may pray despite the need. Similarly, if removing impurity would cause missing the prayer, one may pray with the minor impurity.
This exception is derived from the principle of necessity (darurah) and avoiding hardship.

Source Text

وجه : (۱) پیشاب، پیخانہ کے وقت نماز مکروہ ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ قالت عائشة ) اجلس يا غندرانی رسول الله الله يقول لا صلاة بحضرة الطعام و لا هو يدافعه الاخبثان ۔(مسلم شریف ، باب كراهة الصلاة بحضرة الطعام، الخ، ص ۲۲۶، نمبر ۱۲۴۶/۵۶۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پیشاب پیخانہ کے زور کے وقت نماز نہ پڑھے۔(۲) پہلے ضرورت پوری کرے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال قال النبی الله اذا كان احدكم على الطعام فلا يعجل حتى يقضى حاجته منه و ان اقيمت الصلاة - ( بخاری شریف، باب اذ احضر الطعام وا قیمت الصلاة ،ص ۱۰۹، نمبر ۶۷۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ کھانے یا پیشاب پینانے کی ضرورت ہو تو پہلے اس کو پوری کرو چاہے اقامت کہی جارہی ہو۔(۳)
اور نجاست غلیظہ ایک درہم معاف ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابی ھریرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : تعاد الصلوة من قدر الدرهم من الدم (دار قطنی ، باب قدر النجاسة التي تبطل الصلوۃ ص ۳۸۵ نمبر ۱۴۷۹ سفن سبيع ، ج اول ص ۵۶۶، نمبر ۴۰۹۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ خون یا اس جیسی نجاست غلیظہ درہم سے کم ہو تو معاف ہے۔
درہم کا حساب
درھم کے بارے میں دوستم کی باتیں ہیں ، ایک یہ کہ اسکے وزن کا اعتبار کیا جائے اور دوسری یہ کہ اسکی مساحت یعنی رقبے کا اعتبار کیا جائے تو دونوں قولوں میں ترتیب یہ ہے کہ جس قول میں مساحت کا اعتبار کیا گیا ہے وہ پہلی نجاست کے بارے میں ہے۔ کہ پتلی نجاست ہو تو درھم کے رقبے کا اعتبار کیا جائے اور 2.75 سینٹی میٹر نجاست ہو تو جگہ نا پاک ہوگی ، اور جس قول میں وزن کا اعتبار ہے اسکا مطلب یہ ہے کہ نجاست گاڑھی ہو تو درھم کے وزن کا اعتبار کیا جائے اور 4.374 گرام وزن نجاست ہو تو جگہ نا پاک قراردی جائے چاہے رقبے کے اعتبار سے 2.75 سینٹی میٹر سے کم رقبے پر ہی نجاست لگی ہو۔ یہ انگلینڈ میں پچاس پینس کی مقدار ہے۔
And when one is repelling one of the two evils (urine or stool) or wind, and with impurity that is not preventive (i.e., minor), unless he fears the loss of time or congregation. Commentary: Praying in the middle of the road causes hardship to people so it is disliked. A bathhouse or near a toilet usually has impurity so it is disliked. Graveyard: danger of asking from the dead, so disliked. Praying on another's land without permission is disliked because it is not his land, but if the owner is not displeased it is permissible. Near impurity is disliked because it is not good to worship near it.
Translation (567): And praying while needing to pass urine, stool, or wind, and with non-preventing impurity, unless one fears loss of time or congregation; otherwise it is recommended to cut it (the prayer). Commentary: If one is strongly pressed for urine, stool, or wind, he should relieve himself first. If he fears losing the congregation or time and the need is not severe, he may pray first. Second issue: if one has impurity that is excusable (less than dirham), prayer is valid but disliked; should wash it off. Less than a dirham of thin impurity is excused in area; thick impurity is excused in weight.
Proof (1): For praying while needing to relieve oneself, the hadith: Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) said: 'Sit, O Ghulam [؟], the Messenger of Allah said: There is no prayer when food is present nor when one is repelling the two evils.' (Muslim, chapter on dislike of prayer in presence of food, p. 226 no. 1246/560). This hadith means do not pray when pressed for urine/stool. (2) The hadith: Ibn Umar said the Prophet said: When one of you is eating, do not be hasty until he finishes his need, even if the prayer has been established. (Bukhari, chapter when food is brought and prayer established, p. 109 no. 674) This hadith means: if one needs food or relieving himself, fulfill the need first even if the iqamah is said.
And for thick impurity less than a dirham being excused, the hadith: From Abu Hurairah from the Prophet: The prayer should be repeated (or is invalid) from the amount of a dirham of blood. (Darqutni, chapter on amount of impurity that invalidates prayer, p. 385 no. 1479). This hadith shows that blood or similar thick impurity less than a dirham is excused.
Calculation of dirham: There are two sayings about the dirham: one considers weight, the other considers area. The order is: the saying considering area applies to thin impurity: if thin impurity covers an area of 2.75 cm, the place is impure. The saying considering weight applies to thick impurity: if thick impurity weighs 4.374 grams, the place is impure, even if the area is less than 2.75 cm. This is the amount of fifty pence in England.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage covers two interrelated rulings: (a) praying while in need of relieving oneself, and (b) praying with a minor amount of impurity. The Hanafi position is that both are makruh tanzihi unless one fears missing the time or congregation. The proofs are: the hadith of Aisha on no prayer when repelling the two evils, and the hadith of Ibn Umar on prioritizing need. For impurity, the hadith of Abu Hurairah sets the limit of a dirham for thick impurity (blood). The commentary then explains the dirham calculation: for thin (liquid) impurity, area is considered (approx. 2.75 cm diameter); for thick (solid) impurity, weight is considered (approx. 4.374 grams). This is a crucial practical detail for worshippers.

Key Terms
الاخبثان (al-akhbathan): The two evils: urine and stool.
نجاسة غير مانعة (najasah ghayr mani'ah): Impurity that does not prevent the validity of prayer (less than the excused amount).
درهم (dirham): A silver coin; in fiqh it is a unit of measurement for impurity exemption.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on praying while strongly needing to urinate but fearing loss of congregation?
A) Haram – must relieve himself first
B) Makruh – should relieve himself unless congregation will be lost
C) Permissible without dislike
D) Invalid – prayer not accepted

Key Takeaway
Prayer while suppressing natural needs or with minor impurity is valid but disliked; the dislike lifts when necessity dictates, and the dirham exemption sets a precise boundary for excused impurity.

Salah — Prayer

Prayer Attire: Ruling on Work Clothes and Uncovered Head
Rulings on prayer attire with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying in shabby clothes and with uncovered head, and identify the exception for humility.

Core Idea
Prayer in shabby clothes or with uncovered head is makruh tanzihi unless humility is intended.

In this lesson, we examine two common scenarios related to a person's appearance during prayer: wearing ordinary or shabby work clothes, and praying with an uncovered head. The Hanafi school considers these acts makruh tanzihi (disliked but not sinful) unless there is a valid reason, such as intending humility or having no alternative. The proofs come from prophetic hadith and a Quranic principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts under discussion
The passage addresses two situations: (1) praying in thiyab al-badhlah (ordinary/shabby clothes) and (2) praying with uncovered head (makshuf al-ra's). Note the condition: 'la li al-tadhallul' (not for humility).
The text explicitly excludes the case where uncovering is for humility.
2
State the ruling for each case
Both are makruh tanzihi. That means the prayer is valid but it is disliked to do so without necessity. The ruling is derived from the hadith encouraging proper attire for prayer.
Makruh tanzihi does not invalidate the prayer but one should avoid it.
3
Analyze the hadith proofs
The author cites two hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud: (1) The Prophet encouraged wearing two garments and prohibited wrapping like Jews when only one garment is available. (2) The Prophet forbade praying in a cloak without wrapping it and forbade praying in trousers without a cloak. These indicate the desirability of proper covering.
The hadith are ahad (zanni al-thubut), so the ruling is at the level of makruh tanzihi, not haram.
4
Understand the exception for humility
The commentary clarifies that if one uncovers his head to express humility and supplication, it is permissible. This is based on the Quranic verse 'take your adornment' (7:31) understood as covering for dignity, but humility overrides.
This exception shows the flexibility within the Hanafi school.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider covering the head for men to be sunnah muakkadah, while some view it as wajib. The Hanafi position is that it is not wajib but recommended; omitting it without excuse is makruh.
The difference stems from interpretation of 'adornment' in the Quran.

Source Text

And for the congregation and otherwise it is recommended to cut them (i.e., the need) (568) And prayer in ordinary clothes (569) and with uncovered head without humility.
For al-Bayhaqi, chapter on what necessitates washing from blood.
Translation (568): In working (ordinary) clothes. Commentary: A garment in which it would be disliked to go before respectable people is called 'thiyab al-badhlah'. Praying in it without necessity is makruh.
Proof: (a) Ibn Umar said: The Messenger of Allah (or Umar said): If one of you has two garments, let him pray in both. If he has only one, let him wrap it around his waist and not drape it like the Jews. (Abu Dawud, chapter on when the garment is tight, p. 102 no. 636) This hadith means: if one has two garments, he should wear both; if not, there is an excuse. (2) Abdullah ibn Buraidah from his father: The Prophet forbade praying in a cloak without wrapping it, and forbade praying in trousers without a cloak. (Abu Dawud, same reference) This hadith means: praying only in trousers is not good.
Translation (569): And with uncovered head without humility [is disliked]. Commentary: If one leaves his head uncovered for the purpose of humility and supplication, it is permissible. Otherwise, under normal circumstances, one should cover his head, whether with a cap, scarf, or turban. These are adornments for men, and the verse [O children of Adam, take your adornment]
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage addresses two appearance-related rulings in prayer: (1) praying in ordinary or shabby clothes (thiyab al-badhlah) and (2) praying with uncovered head without the intent of humility. The Hanafi ruling is that both are makruh tanzihi unless there is a valid reason. For clothing, the hadith from Abu Dawud encourages wearing two garments and condemns praying only in trousers. For head covering, the norm is that men should cover their heads for prayer as it is adornment and respect; uncovering without humility is disliked. However, if one uncovers to express humility, it is allowed. The passage references the Quranic verse 'take your adornment' to support head covering.

Key Terms
ثياب البذلة (thiyab al-badhlah): Ordinary, work, or shabby clothes that one would not wear in front of respectable people.
مكشوف الرأس (makshuf al-ra's): Uncovered head; for men, it is disliked unless done for humility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) When done for humility and supplication

D) When it is very hot

Key Takeaway
Both praying in shabby clothes and with uncovered head without humility are makruh tanzihi in the Hanafi school, but exceptions for necessity and humility render them permissible.

Praying in Ordinary Clothes (Thiyab al-Badhlah)
First of three disliked acts: clothing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying in thiyab al-badhlah and identify the hadith evidence that establishes it as makruh tanzihi.

Core Idea
Praying in working clothes that you would not wear to visit respectable people is disliked unless necessary.

This lesson focuses on one of the disliked acts in prayer: wearing thiyab al-badhlah (ordinary, working clothes). The Hanafi school, relying on prophetic practice and explicit hadiths, considers it better to wear proper attire for prayer, as prayer is a dignified act of worship. Understanding this ruling helps the believer refine the quality of their salah.

Guided Path
1
Become acquainted with the term and its definition
Identify the term 'thiyab al-badhlah' and understand what kind of clothing it refers to: clothes that are so ordinary that one would feel hesitant to visit respectable people in them.
2
State the ruling and its hukm level
Determine the legal classification: makruh tanzihi (disliked, not prohibited). The prayer is still valid but it is better to avoid. Note the exception: when there is a necessity (e.g., no other clothes), it is not disliked.
3
Examine the key hadith evidence
Read the hadith from Ibn Umar recommending two garments and forbidding the Jewish manner of wrapping; and the hadith forbidding prayer in a single blanket without wrapping and in trousers without a cloak. Understand how these proofs indicate dislike for insufficient or ordinary clothing.
The hadith are from Abu Dawud, classified as ahad, zanni in transmission and meaning.
4
Apply the ruling to contemporary scenarios
Consider modern equivalents: wearing a shabby or overly casual outfit (e.g., gym clothes) in prayer when better clothes are available. The ruling also applies to clothes with logos or images that might be disrespectful? But the focus here is on the nature of the garment itself.

(آیت ۳۱ سورۃ الاعراف ۷ ) فرمایا، کہ نماز کے وقت زینت اختیار کرو۔ ایک زمانے میں پگڑی کا رواج تھا ابھی اس کی جگہ پر ٹوپی ، یارو مال کا رواج ہے۔ صلى الله عليه وسلم على المنبر و عليه عمامة سوداء قد ارخی طرفها بين كتفيه (ابوداود شریف، باب فی العمائم ، ص ۵۷۴، نمبر ۷ ۴۰ شمائل ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی عمامۃ النبی ص۸)(۲) عن ابن عباس ان النبي الا اللهم خطب الناس و عليه عصابة دسماء ۔ (شمائل ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی عمامہ النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم ، ص ۸ نمبر ) ان دونوں حدیثوں میں ہے کہ خطبہ کے وقت حضور پگڑی پہنے ہوئے تھے ۔(۳) عن جابر قال دخل النبي الله مكة يوم الفتح و عليه عمامة سوداء - ( ترمذی شریف باب ما جاء فى لبس الصوف ،ص ۱۴۱۴، نمبر ۱۷۳۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضرت موسی علیہ السلام اون کی ٹوپی پہنے تھے۔ اس لئے ٹوپی پہننا چاہئے ۔ (1) عن هلال بن يساف قال .... قلت لصاحبي نبدأ فننظر الى دله فاذا عليه قلنسوة لاطية ذات اذنين ۔(ابوداود شریف ، باب الرجل يعتمد في الصلاة على عصابص ۱۴۴، نمبر ۹۴۸) اس عمل صحابی میں ہے کہ ان پر نماز میں ٹوپی تھی۔ (۷) قال الحسن كان القوم يسجدون على العمامة و القلنسوة ويداه في كمه ( بخاری شریف، باب السجود وعلى الثوب في شدة الحرص ۲۸، نمبر ۳۸۵) اس قول صحابی کے اشارے سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ وہ حضرات عمامہ اور ٹوپی پہنا کرتے تھے۔ (۶) قال ركانة و سمعت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول فرق ما بيننا و بين المشركين العمائم على القلانس ۔ (ابوداود شریف ، باب فی العمائم ، ص ۵۷۴، نمبر۴۰۷۷) اس حدیث میں پگڑی اور اس کے نیچے ٹوپی دونوں کا ثبوت ہے۔ ترجمه : (۵۷۰) کھانا موجود ہو اس طرح کہ دل اس کی طرف مائل ہو اور مشغول ہو جائے اور خشوع میں خلل انداز ہو جائے تو [ تو مکروہ ہے]
Translation: (568) [Prayer] in common clothes. Explanation: Such clothes that cause dislike when going to good people are called 'thiyab al-badhlah'. Praying in them without necessity is disliked. Evidence: (1) Ibn Umar: The Prophet said... (2) Abdullah ibn Buraidah: The Prophet forbade praying in a blanket without wrapping and in trousers without a cloak. Translation: (569) And with uncovered head without humility [is disliked]. Explanation: If one removes head covering for humility and supplication, it is permissible; otherwise, covering the head is required, whether cap, turban, etc., as adornment for men. The verse 'O Children of Adam, take your adornment at every masjid' (7:31) commands adornment. Then hadith on the Prophet's turban and cap. Translation: (570) And in the presence of food to which one is inclined and which occupies the mind and spoils khushu', [it is disliked].
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on three disliked acts (makruhat) in prayer from the Hanafi school. First, praying in ordinary clothes (thiyab al-badhlah) that one would not wear to visit respectable people is disliked unless necessary. Proofs from hadith indicate that wearing two garments is better, and praying only in a lower garment is disliked. Second, praying with an uncovered head without the intention of humility is disliked; covering the head (with a cap, turban, etc.) is a sign of adornment and is recommended, supported by many hadith showing the Prophet's practice and that of the Companions. Third, praying when food is present and one is inclined to it is disliked because it distracts from khushu'. The ruling is clear: one should eat first if food is ready and one desires it.

Key Terms
ثیاب البذلہ (thiyab al-badhlah): Ordinary, working clothes that one would not wear to visit respectable people.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling for praying in thiyab al-badhlah without necessity?
A) Haram
B) Makruh tanzihi
C) Mustahab
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Praying in ordinary work clothes without a valid excuse is disliked (makruh tanzihi) because proper attire enhances the dignity and khushu' of prayer.

Salah — Prayer
beginner

Praying with Uncovered Head (for Men)
Second disliked act: head covering

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on praying with an uncovered head for men, distinguish between disliked and permissible cases, and cite the relevant proofs.

Core Idea
Covering the head is a form of adornment and humility; leaving it uncovered without a valid reason is disliked.

This lesson addresses the second disliked act: praying with an uncovered head (for men) without humility and supplication. The Hanafi school recommends covering the head with a cap, turban, or any cloth, as it is part of the adornment (zinah) commanded in the Quran. However, if one uncovers the head intentionally to show humility (tadhallul), it is permitted and even virtuous.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying with uncovered head (makshuf al-ra's) for men. The ruling is makruh tanzihi when done without a reason like tadhallul (humility).
2
Understand the exception
If a person intentionally uncovers the head to express humility and dependence on Allah (tadhallul), it is not disliked; rather, it is commendable. The general dislike is for routine uncovering without such intention.
3
Examine the evidence from Quran and Sunnah
The verse 'O Children of Adam, take your adornment at every place of prayer' (7:31) is cited. The evidence includes multiple hadith showing the Prophet's practice of wearing a turban and cap, and the Companions' practice.
The proofs are many; the lesson focuses on the Hanafi interpretation that head covering is part of zinah.
4
Apply the ruling to daily life
A man should wear a cap, turban, or at least a handkerchief on his head during prayer if available. If he intentionally removes it for humility, it is fine; otherwise, it is disliked.

Praying While Food is Present
Third disliked act: presence of food

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying when food that one desires is present and explain its basis in preserving khushu'.

Core Idea
If food is ready and you are inclined to eat, pray after eating to prevent distraction from khushu'.

The third disliked act concerns praying when food is present and one is inclined to it. The Hanafi school, focusing on the objective of khushu' (focus and humility), teaches that one should not start prayer while desiring food, as the mind will be occupied. Better to eat first if time permits, then pray with full concentration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the reason for dislike
The act is beginning prayer when food is served and one has an appetite for it. The reason is that it distracts the mind and spoils khushu'.
2
Determine the hukm and its nuance
The ruling is makruh tanzihi. It applies when the food is present and one's inclination is strong enough to disturb focus. If one can maintain khushu', it is not disliked.
3
Examine the evidence from hadith
The text does not explicitly cite a hadith here (the source passage ends with the statement and reference to khushu'). The ruling is based on the principle of avoiding distractions and is supported by hadith such as 'If the evening meal is served, begin with it before praying' (Bukhari).
4
Apply the ruling to modern settings
If you are at a gathering and food is placed, it is better to eat first (if the prayer time is not about to expire) and then pray. likewise, if you are at home and your meal is ready, do not postpone it to pray if you will be distracted.

(آیت ۳۱ سورۃ الاعراف ۷ ) فرمایا، کہ نماز کے وقت زینت اختیار کرو۔ ایک زمانے میں پگڑی کا رواج تھا ابھی اس کی جگہ پر ٹوپی ، یارو مال کا رواج ہے۔ صلى الله عليه وسلم على المنبر و عليه عمامة سوداء قد ارخی طرفها بين كتفيه (ابوداود شریف، باب فی العمائم ، ص ۵۷۴، نمبر ۷ ۴۰ شمائل ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی عمامۃ النبی ص۸)(۲) عن ابن عباس ان النبي الا اللهم خطب الناس و عليه عصابة دسماء ۔ (شمائل ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی عمامہ النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم ، ص ۸ نمبر ) ان دونوں حدیثوں میں ہے کہ خطبہ کے وقت حضور پگڑی پہنے ہوئے تھے ۔(۳) عن جابر قال دخل النبي الله مكة يوم الفتح و عليه عمامة سوداء - ( ترمذی شریف باب ما جاء فی العمامة السوداء، ص ۴۱۴، نمبر ۱۷۳۵ را بو داود شریف ، باب فی العمائم، ص ۵۷۴، نمبر ۴۰۷۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ پگڑی پہننا چاہئے ۔ (۴) عـــن ابـــن عمر قال كان النبى الله الله اذا اعتم سدل عمامته بين كتفيه - ( ترمذی شریف ، باب فی سدل العمامة بين الله الكتفين ص ۲۱۴، نمبر ۱۷۳۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ پگڑی کا شملہ کندھوں کے درمیان لڑکا نا چاہئے ۔ (۵) عن ابن مسعود عن النبی قال كان على موسى يوم كلمه ربه كساء صوف وجبة صوف و كمة صوف و سراويل صوف و كانت نعلاه من جلد حمار ميت ..... و الكمة القلنسوة الصغيرة - ( ترمذی شریف باب ما جاء فى لبس الصوف ،ص ۱۴۱۴، نمبر ۱۷۳۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضرت موسی علیہ السلام اون کی ٹوپی پہنے تھے۔ اس لئے ٹوپی پہننا چاہئے ۔ (1) عن هلال بن يساف قال .... قلت لصاحبي نبدأ فننظر الى دله فاذا عليه قلنسوة لاطية ذات اذنين ۔(ابوداود شریف ، باب الرجل يعتمد في الصلاة على عصابص ۱۴۴، نمبر ۹۴۸) اس عمل صحابی میں ہے کہ ان پر نماز میں ٹوپی تھی۔ (۷) قال الحسن كان القوم يسجدون على العمامة و القلنسوة ويداه في كمه ( بخاری شریف، باب السجود وعلى الثوب في شدة الحرص ۲۸، نمبر ۳۸۵) اس قول صحابی کے اشارے سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ وہ حضرات عمامہ اور ٹوپی پہنا کرتے تھے۔ (۶) قال ركانة و سمعت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول فرق ما بيننا و بين المشركين العمائم على القلانس ۔ (ابوداود شریف ، باب فی العمائم ، ص ۵۷۴، نمبر۴۰۷۷) اس حدیث میں پگڑی اور اس کے نیچے ٹوپی دونوں کا ثبوت ہے۔ ترجمه : (۵۷۰) کھانا موجود ہو اس طرح کہ دل اس کی طرف مائل ہو اور مشغول ہو جائے اور خشوع میں خلل انداز ہو جائے تو [ تو مکروہ ہے]
Translation: (568) [Prayer] in common clothes. Explanation: Such clothes that cause dislike when going to good people are called 'thiyab al-badhlah'. Praying in them without necessity is disliked. Evidence: (1) Ibn Umar: The Prophet said... (2) Abdullah ibn Buraidah: The Prophet forbade praying in a blanket without wrapping and in trousers without a cloak. Translation: (569) And with uncovered head without humility [is disliked]. Explanation: If one removes head covering for humility and supplication, it is permissible; otherwise, covering the head is required, whether cap, turban, etc., as adornment for men. The verse 'O Children of Adam, take your adornment at every masjid' (7:31) commands adornment. Then hadith on the Prophet's turban and cap. Translation: (570) And in the presence of food to which one is inclined and which occupies the mind and spoils khushu', [it is disliked].
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on three disliked acts (makruhat) in prayer from the Hanafi school. First, praying in ordinary clothes (thiyab al-badhlah) that one would not wear to visit respectable people is disliked unless necessary. Proofs from hadith indicate that wearing two garments is better, and praying only in a lower garment is disliked. Second, praying with an uncovered head without the intention of humility is disliked; covering the head (with a cap, turban, etc.) is a sign of adornment and is recommended, supported by many hadith showing the Prophet's practice and that of the Companions. Third, praying when food is present and one is inclined to it is disliked because it distracts from khushu'. The ruling is clear: one should eat first if food is ready and one desires it.

Key Terms
خشوع (khushu'): Humility and focus in prayer; its disturbance makes a disliked act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it disliked to pray in the presence of food?
A) When food is present, regardless of one's desire.
B) Only when one is extremely hungry.
C) When one's inclination to the food disturbs khushu'.
D) It is never disliked.

Key Takeaway
Prayer should not be performed when one is distracted by the presence of desirable food; eat first to ensure khushu'.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Praying When Food Is Present and the Recommendation of Head Cover
Ruling with proof for food and head cover

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying when food is present with severe hunger, and explain the evidence for wearing a turban or cap during prayer.

Core Idea
Praying with severe hunger in the presence of food is disliked because it disrupts khushu; wearing proper head cover is a recommended adornment.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah addresses two interrelated aspects of prayer etiquette: the prohibition of praying when distracted by food, and the encouragement to adorn oneself for prayer, particularly by covering the head with a turban or cap. The author provides a detailed proof chain for both rulings, grounding them in Quran and Sunnah. Understanding these rulings helps the believer achieve khushu and follow the prophetic practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying while food is present and one is intensely hungry. The Hanafi ruling is makruh tanzih (disliked but not sinful).
If hunger is not severe, no dislike.
2
Locate the dalil for the food ruling
Two hadith are cited: (1) Aisha’s report: 'There is no prayer in the presence of food' (Muslim). (2) Ibn Umar’s report: 'Eat first even if the prayer has been called' (Bukhari). These indicate the recommendation to eat first and that prayer with food is incomplete in perfection.
Hanafi scholars interpret 'la salata' as 'no perfect prayer'.
3
Understand the ikhtilaf and the Hanafi response
Some other schools consider praying while hungry as merely permissible. The Hanafi response is that the hadith explicitly advises eating first, implying dislike when khushu is lost.
Thamarah al-khilaf: In Hanafi, eat first; other schools allow praying while hungry.
4
Analyze the adornment proof
The Quranic verse 'Take your adornment at every mosque' (7:31) is interpreted as a recommendation for head cover. The author then lists eight hadith showing the Prophet and Companions wearing turban and cap during prayer, establishing that this is the sunnah.
Adornment includes proper head covering.
5
Apply the ruling
One should eat first if hungry, and wear a turban or cap for prayer as an expression of zinat. The dislikedness is conditioned on intense hunger; otherwise it is not disliked.
Practical takeaway: prioritized eating over prayer when hungry for khushu.

وجه : (۱) بھوک تیز ہونے کے وقت نماز مکروہ ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ قالت عائشة ) اجلس يا غندر انى سمعت رسول الله الله يقول لا صلاة بحضرة الطعام ولا هو يدافعه الاخبثان (مسلم شریف ، باب کراھة الصلاة بحضرة الطعام ، الخ، ص ۲۲۶، نمبر ۱۲۴۶/۵۶۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ کھانے کے وقت نماز نہ پڑھے۔ (۲) پہلے کھانا کھائے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال قال النبى الله اذا كان احدكم على الطعام فلا يعجل حتى يقضي حاجته منه و ان اقيمت الصلاة - ( بخاری شریف ، باب اذ احضر الطعام واقیمت الصلاۃ ص ۱۰۹، نمبر ۶۷۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ کھانے یا پیشاب پینانے کی ضرورت ہو تو پہلے اس کو پوری کرو چاہے اقامت کہی جارہی ہو۔
لغت : بذلته : خرچ، یاب البذلة : ایسا کپڑا جس میں آدمی محنت مزدوری کرتا ہو۔ تذلل : ذلیل ہونا ، آہ وزاری کرنا۔ التضرع: گڑ گڑانا۔ البال: دل، ایشغل البال: جو دل کو مشغول کرے۔
Chapter: What is disliked for the one praying and supplicating. (570) And in the presence of food to which he inclines, and whatever occupies the mind and disrupts khushu at every mosque. (Verse 31 of Surah al-A'raf) He said: At the time of prayer, adopt adornment. Once upon a time, wearing a turban was customary; now in its place, cap or something else is customary. Hadiths on the turban and cap. Proof: (1) From Ja'far ibn 'Umar ibn Hurayth from his father: 'I saw the Prophet on the pulpit wearing a black turban, letting its end hang between his shoulders.' (Abu Dawud, Bab fil-'Ama'im, p. 574, no. 740; Shama'il al-Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi 'amamat al-nabi, p. 8) (2) From Ibn 'Abbas: 'The Prophet addressed the people wearing a dark-colored turban.' (Shama'il al-Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi 'amamat al-nabi, p. 8) These two hadith show that the Prophet wore a turban during the sermon. (3) From Jabir: 'The Prophet entered Mecca on the Day of Conquest wearing a black turban.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fil-'amamat al-sawda', p. 414, no. 1735; Abu Dawud, Bab fil-'Ama'im, p. 574, no. 4077) This hadith indicates that one should wear a turban. (4) From Ibn 'Umar: 'When the Prophet wore a turban, he let its tail hang between his shoulders.' (Tirmidhi, Bab fi sadl al-'amamat bayn al-katifayn, p. 214, no. 1736) This hadith shows that the turban's tail should be left between the shoulders. (5) From Ibn Mas'ud from the Prophet: 'On the day Musa was spoken to by his Lord, he wore a woolen cloak, a woolen jubba, a woolen cap, and woolen trousers, and his sandals were from the skin of a dead donkey... and al-kummah is the small cap.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi lubs al-suf, p. 1414, no. 1734) This hadith shows that Prophet Musa wore a woolen cap, so one should wear a cap. (1) From Hilal ibn Yasaf: 'I said to my companion: Let us begin and look at his house; there was a lapping cap with two ears.' (Abu Dawud, Bab al-rajul ya'tamid fi al-salat 'ala 'asan, p. 144, no. 948) This action of a Companion shows that he had a cap on in prayer. (7) Al-Hasan said: 'The people used to prostrate while wearing the turban and cap, and their hands were in their sleeves.' (Bukhari, Bab al-sujud wa 'ala al-thawb fi shidda al-harr, p. 28, no. 385) This statement of a Companion indicates that they used to wear turban and cap. (6) Rukana said: 'I heard the Prophet say: The distinction between us and the polytheists is the turbans over the caps.' (Abu Dawud, Bab fil-'Ama'im, p. 574, no. 4077) This hadith proves both the turban and the cap underneath. Translation: (570) When food is present such that the heart inclines towards it and becomes occupied, and khushu is disrupted, then [it is disliked]. Then: Chapter: What is disliked for the one praying. (571) Counting verses and tasbih with the hand. (572[a]) The imam standing in the mihrab or on a raised place or on the ground. Explanation: Food is present and one is so hungry that the heart inclines towards it and khushu and khudu' disappear from the prayer. In such a case, praying is disliked. And if the hunger is not severe, it is not disliked. Proof: (1) There is a hadith for the dislike of praying when hunger is severe: 'Aisha said: Sit down, O Ghundar, for I heard the Messenger of Allah say: There is no prayer in the presence of food nor when one is repressing the two impurities.' (Muslim, Bab karahat al-salat bi hadarat al-ta'am, etc., p. 226, no. 1246/560) This hadith says do not pray during food. (2) Eat first. For this there is a hadith: Ibn 'Umar said: The Prophet said: When one of you is at food, let him not be hasty until he fulfills his need from it, even if the prayer has been called.' (Bukhari, Bab idha hadara al-ta'am wa uqimat al-salat, p. 109, no. 647) This hadith says that if you need food or to relieve yourself, first complete that even if the iqamah is being said. Lexicon: Badhlah: expenditure. Yab al-badhlah: a garment in which a person does hard work. Tadhallul: being lowly, lamentation. Al-tadarru': begging. Al-bal: heart. 'Yashghal al-bal': that which occupies the heart.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It discusses the dislike (karahah) of praying when food is present and one desires it, and when the heart is distracted from khushu. The author begins with a chapter heading and then provides the matn: 'And in the presence of food to which he inclines, and whatever occupies the mind and disrupts khushu at every mosque.' He then quotes the Quranic verse 'Take your adornment at every mosque' (7:31) to emphasize that one should dress nicely for prayer. This leads to a lengthy discussion on the importance of wearing a turban and cap during prayer, providing several hadith to prove that these were the practice of the Prophet and the Companions. He lists eight proofs: (1) the Prophet wore a black turban on the pulpit, (2) he wore a dark turban during a sermon, (3) he wore a black turban on the Day of Conquest, (4) he let the turban tail hang between his shoulders, (5) Prophet Musa wore a woolen cap, (6) a Companion (Hilal ibn Yasaf) wore a cap in prayer, (7) the Companions used to prostrate with turban and cap, and (8) the Prophet said the distinction is turbans over caps. These establish that covering the head with a turban and cap is a recommended adornment (zinat) for prayer, fulfilling the Quranic command. Then he gives the translation of ruling (570): prayer is disliked when food is present and the heart inclines to it, disrupting khushu. On the next page, he clarifies that the dislike applies only when hunger is strong; if not, it is not disliked. He provides two hadith: one from Aisha that there is no prayer with food present (meaning the prayer is invalid in the sense of not being perfect), and one from Ibn 'Umar that one should eat first even if the prayer has begun. He then gives a lexicon of related terms. The key point is that the Hanafi school considers praying with strong hunger in the presence of food as makruh tanzihi, because it prevents proper khushu. The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah, with proofs from hadith.

Key Terms
خشوع (khushu'): Humility and concentration in prayer
زینت (zinat): Adornment, including proper clothing like turban and cap for prayer
عمامة ('amama): Turban, a headwrap
قلنسوة (qalansuwa): Cap (skullcap) worn under turban

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it makruh to pray in the presence of food according to this passage?
A) Whenever food is present, regardless of hunger level
B) Only when one is intensely hungry and desires the food
C) Only when the food is delicious
D) Only during Ramadan

Key Takeaway
Praying while intensely hungry in the presence of food is makruh tanzih because it disrupts khushu; wearing a turban and cap is a recommended sunnah based on the Quranic command of adornment and prophetic practice.
